Ijarah — Hire and Lease
beginner
6 min
General Permissibility of Land Ijarah
States general permissibility and validity of diverse land ijarah contracts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that land ijarah is not limited to cultivation and identify the conditions for a valid lease.

Core Idea
Land can be leased for any lawful benefit, not just farming.

Many assume land ijarah is only for agriculture, but Hanafi fiqh allows a wide range of uses. This lesson clarifies the general principle and its modern application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the misconception
Recognize that some texts may imply ijarah is only for farming, but the author refutes this.
2
State the general rule
From al-Hidayah and Ghayat al-Bayan: land can be leased for cultivation, building, planting, baking bricks, etc.
The examples show the scope of permissible uses.
3
Apply to a modern scenario
Leasing land as a resting place (maqil/marah) is valid if the lessor provides the empty land and the lessee can use it for any purpose.
Even if water covers the land, it is not a defect that voids the contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن الأرض لا ينحصر استئجارها للزراعة والبناء والغرس كما توهمه المتون فقد صرح في الهداية بأن الأرض تستأجر للزراعة وغيرها. وقال في غاية البيان: أراد بغير الزراعة البناء والغرس وطبخ والآجر والخزف ونحو ذلك من سائر الانتفاعات بالأرض اهـ . فإذا عرفت ذلك ظهر لك صحة الإجارات الواقعة في زماننا من أنه يستأجر الأرض مقيلاً ومراحاً قاصداً بذلك إلزام الأجرة بالتمكن منها مطلقاً، سواء شملها الماء وأمكن زراعتها أولاً، ولا شك في صحته لأنه لم يستأجرها للزراعة بخصوصها حتى يكون عدم ريها عيباً تنفسخ به. وفي الولوالجية : استأجر أرضاً ليلبن فيها فالإجارة فاسدة ثم هي على وجهين: إن كان للتراب قيمة ضمن قيمته وبكون اللبن له وإن لم يكن له قيمة فلا شيء عليه واللبن له وضمن نقصان الأرض إن نقصت وفي فتاوى قارئ الهداية : إن إجارة الأرض المشغولة بزرع الغير إن كان الزرع بحق بأن كان بأجرة لا يجوز أن يؤجر ما لم يستحصد الزرع إلا أن يؤجرها مضافة إلى المستقبل، وإن كان الزرع بغير مستند شرعي صحت الإجارة لأن الزرع في هذه الصورة واجب القلع فإن المؤجر في هذه الصورة قادر على تسليم ما أجره ويجب صاحب الزرع على قلعه سواء أدرك أم لا لأنه لا حق لصاحبه في إبقائه اهـ. والدار المشغولة بمتاع الساكن الذي ليس بمستأجر تصح إجارتها وابتداء المدة من حين تسليمها فارغة؛ كذا في القنية. وفي الخلاصة ولو أجر الأرض المزروعة ثم سلمه بعدما فرغ وحصد ينقلب جائزاً، ولو قال المستأجر أجرت منك الأرض وهي فارغة وقال المؤجر لا بل هي مشغولة بزرعي بحكم الحال؛ كذا في المنتقى. وفي فتاوى الفضلي: القول قول الآجر اهـ. وللمستأجر الشرب والطريق لأنه لا ينتفع بعقد الإجارة إلا بهما بخلاف المبيع لأن المقصود ملك الرقبة لا الانتفاع ولهذا صح بيع الجحش الصغير والأرض السبخة. وفي شرح الطحاوي : وإن أجر المستأجر بأكثر مما استأجره فإن كانت الأجرة من جنس ما استأجر به ولم يزد في الدار شيئاً لا تطيب له الزيادة ويتصدق بها، فإن زاد شيئاً آخر طابت له الزيادة أو أجر بخلاف جنس ما استأجر به والكنس ليس بزيادة .
Know that leasing land is not restricted to cultivation, building, and planting, as the texts might suggest. Indeed, it is explicitly stated in al-Hidayah that land is leased for cultivation and other purposes. He said in Ghayat al-Bayan: 'By other than cultivation, he meant building, planting, baking bricks and pottery, and similar uses of the land.' End quote. Once you know this, the validity of ijarah contracts in our time becomes clear: that one leases land as a resting place and shelter, intending thereby to obligate the rent by mere availability, whether water covers it and cultivation is possible or not. There is no doubt about its validity because he did not lease it specifically for cultivation such that lack of irrigation would be a defect terminating the contract. In al-Walwaljiyyah: If one leases land to make bricks, the ijarah is void, then it is on two sides: if the soil has value, he guarantees its value and the bricks belong to him; if it has no value, nothing is due on him and the bricks belong to him, and he guarantees any diminution in the land. In Fatawa Qari' al-Hidayah: Leasing land occupied by another's crop: if the crop is there legally (e.g., by rental), it is not permissible to let it until the crop is harvested, unless it is leased for a future period. If the crop is without legal basis, the ijarah is valid because the crop must be uprooted; the lessor can deliver what he leased, and the owner of the crop must uproot it whether ripe or not, since he has no right to keep it. End quote. A house occupied by the belongings of a resident who is not a tenant: its lease is valid, and the term begins from the time it is delivered empty; thus in al-Qunyah. In al-Khulasa: If one leases land that is already sown, then delivers it after it is cleared and harvested, it becomes valid. If the lessee says 'I leased the land from you when it was empty' and the lessor says 'No, it was occupied by my crop, so it is according to the condition', thus in al-Muntaqa. In Fatawa al-Fadli: The word is with the lessor. End quote. The lessee has the right to irrigation and pathway because he cannot benefit from the ijarah contract without them, unlike a sale, because the objective is ownership of the property, not benefit; for this reason, selling a small donkey and saline land is valid. In Sharh al-Tahawi: If the lessee sublets at a higher rent, if the rent is of the same type as what he leased for and he did not add anything to the property, the increase is not permissible for him and he must give it in charity. If he added something else, the increase is permissible for him, or if he sublets for a different type of rent. Sweeping is not an addition.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage clarifies that land can be leased for many purposes beyond farming, including construction and planting. The author refutes a possible misconception that ijarah of land is limited to agriculture. It then presents numerous specific rulings: hiring for brickmaking (fasid but with consequences), leasing occupied land (valid only if the occupant has no legal right), leasing with delayed delivery, disputes over condition at contract time, lessee's rights to water and access, and subletting at a profit. The common theme is that the benefit of land is diverse and the ijarah contract must be analyzed based on the actual benefit and possession. The Hanafi school uses flexible reasoning (istihsan) to validate many contracts that might be invalid by strict analogy.

Key Terms
إجارة (ijarah): Lease contract transferring usufruct of an asset for rent
منفعة (manfa'ah): Benefit or utility derived from the leased asset

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on leasing land as a resting place (maqil) if it is flooded with water?
A) The lease is invalid because the land cannot be used.
B) The lease is valid because the lessee intended only the availability of the land.
C) The lease is valid only if the lessee also intends to plant.
D) The lease is void because water is a defect.

Key Takeaway
Land ijarah in the Hanafi school covers any lawful benefit, not just agriculture, and is valid as long as the lessor can deliver the empty land.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate

Leasing for Building and Planting: Conditions and Post-Term Obligations
Explains the validity of leasing land for building/planting with a specified period and the rules after expiry

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition (specified period) for a valid lease for building/planting, and explain why the lessee must immediately remove improvements after expiry, distinguishing it from cultivation.

Core Idea
Building/planting on leased land requires a fixed term; upon expiry, immediate removal is mandatory because there is no natural end.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses two key rulings: first, the validity of leasing land for building or planting when the period is known, and second, the obligation to remove structures and trees after the lease ends. The commentary contrasts this with cultivation, where crops are left until harvest due to a known end, and uses istihsan to derive the rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main rulings
The passage first states that a lease for building/planting is permissible if the period is specified. Then it rules that after the period expires, the lessee must remove the building and trees and return the land empty. These are the two core legal positions.
The ruling is analogous to leasing for cultivation except for the post-term obligation.
2
Determine the condition for validity
The condition for validity is that the benefit (building/planting) and the period must be known. This is similar to any ijarah: uncertainty in rent or duration invalidates the contract. The text explicitly states 'because the benefit is known and the period is known'.
If the period is not specified, the lease is fasid (voidable).
3
Compare the post-term obligation with cultivation
After expiry, the lessee must immediately remove buildings and trees because they have no natural end. In contrast, if the land was leased for cultivation and the crop is not yet ripe, it is left until harvest with a rental at the like rate. The reason is that cultivation has a known end (harvest), allowing both parties' interests to be balanced.
This is the key distinction: known end vs. no known end.
4
Understand the istihsan reasoning
Qiyas would require immediate removal in all cases, including cultivation, because the land is the owner's property. However, istihsan overrides qiyas for cultivation due to the known end. For building/planting, the qiyas ruling (immediate removal) remains because there is no known end to justify delay.
Istihsan is the preferred reasoning here, not a contradiction of qiyas but a refinement.
5
Apply the rules to special cases
The passage includes two special cases: (1) An invalid sharing arrangement (half land, half trees) results in the landowner owing the value of trees and the worker receiving wages, with no order to uproot. (2) For waqf land, the lessee may retain improvements with rent (istihkar) if there is no harm, even if the beneficiary objects.
These exceptions show the flexibility of Hanafi fiqh to prevent loss.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وللبناء والغرس إن بين مدة يعني جاز استئجار الأرض للبناء والغرس بين مدة لأن المنفعة معلومة والمدة معلومة فتصح كما لو استأجرها للزراعة. وفي المحيط : دفع أرضه لرجل ليغرس أشجاراً على أن تكون الأرض والشجر بينهما نصفين لم يجز والشجر لرب الأرض وعليه قيمة الشجر وله أجر ما عمل ولا يؤمر بقلعه وهذه إجارة فاسدة لأنه جعل أجرة ما يخرج من العمل وعلى رب الأرض قيمة الأشجار لأنه صار مستقرضاً للأشجار منه وتقايضا لها حكماً واستقراض الأشجار لا يجوز فيكون قرضاً فاسداً فيوجب الملك إذا اتصل به القبض. وفي القنية من الوقف ولا يجوز استئجار السبيل ليبني به غرفة لنفسه إلا أن يزيد في الأجرة ولا يضر بالبناء، وإن كان لا يرغب المستأجر إلا على هذا الوقف جاز من غير زيادة في الأجرة إذا قال القيم أو المالك أذنت له في عمارتها فعمر بإذنه يرجع عليه وعلى الوقف. هذا إذا كان يرجع نفعه إلى الوقف والمالك، وإن كان إلى المستأجر وفيه ضرر كالبالوعة والتنور فإنه لا يرجع إلا إذا شرط الرجوع . قال رحمه الله : (فإن مضت المدة قلعهما وسلمها فارغة يعني إذا مضت مدة الإجارة قلع البناء والغرس وسلم الأرض إلى المؤجر فارغة لأنه يجب عليه تفريغها وتسليمها إلى صاحبها فارغة وذلك بقلعها في الحال لأنه ليس له غاية تعلم بخلاف ما إذا كانت للزراعة وانقضت المدة والزرع لم يدرك حيث يترك على حاله إلى الحصاد بأجر المثل لأن له غاية معلومة فأمكن مراعاة الجانبين وبخلاف ما إذا مات أحد المتعاقدين في المدة والزرع لم يدرك بحيث يترك بالأجرة على حاله إلى الحصاد وإن بطلت الإجارة فكان تركه بالمسمى وإبقاء العقد على ما كان أولى من النقض وإعادته، وبخلاف ما إذا غصب أرضاً وزرعها حيث يأمر بالقلع وإن كان له نهاية لأن ابتداء فعله ظلماً وقع والظلم يجب إعدامه لا تقريره والقياس أن يقلع في الأمور كلها لأن الأرض ملكه فلا تؤجر بغير إذنه. ووجه الاستحسان وهو الفرق بين البناء والغرس والزرع ما تقدم. وفي القنية والخصاف: استأجر أرضاً وقفاً ليبني فيها أو يغرس ثم مضت مدة الإجارة فللمستأجر أن يستبقيها بأجرة المثل إذا لم يكن في ذلك ضرر، ولو أبي الموقوف عليه إلا القلع فليس له ذلك علم حكم الاستحكار وهذا وارد على إطلاق المؤلف. وفي المحيط : وإذا اهـ. ومن هنا
He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (And for building and planting, if a period is specified) meaning it is permissible to lease land for building and planting if a period is specified, because the benefit is known and the period is known, so it becomes valid as if he leased it for cultivation. In al-Muhit: He gave his land to a man to plant trees on condition that the land and trees be shared equally; it is not permissible. The trees belong to the owner of the land, and he must pay their value, and the worker is entitled to his wages, and he is not ordered to uproot them. This is a void ijarah because he made the wages what comes out of the work. The owner of the land must pay the value of the trees because he becomes a borrower of the trees from him, and they exchange ownership effectively. Borrowing trees is not permissible, so it is a void loan that results in ownership when possession is taken. In al-Qunyah from the chapter on waqf: It is not permissible to lease a resthouse (sabil) to build a room for himself unless he increases the rent and does not harm the building. If the lessee is not interested except in this waqf, it is permissible without an increase in rent if the trustee or owner says 'I permitted him to repair it' and he repaired with permission; then he may seek recourse from him and from the waqf. This applies if the benefit reverts to the waqf and the owner. If the benefit is for the lessee and there is harm like a cesspit or oven, then he has no recourse unless the condition of recourse was stipulated. He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (If the period expires, he removes them both and returns the land empty) meaning when the period of ijarah expires, he removes the building and trees and returns the land to the lessor empty, because he must empty it and deliver it to its owner empty. This is done by removing them immediately because there is no known end. Unlike the case of cultivation where the period ends and the crop has not ripened: it is left as is until harvest with a rental at the like rate, because it has a known end, so it is possible to consider both sides. Also unlike the case where one of the contracting parties dies during the period and the crop has not ripened: it is left with the rent as is until harvest, even if the ijarah becomes void, leaving it with the named rent and upholding the contract is preferable to rescinding and reinstating it. Also unlike the case of usurpation of land and planting there: he is ordered to uproot even if there is an end, because his initial act was unjust, and injustice must be removed, not confirmed. Qiyas would require uprooting in all cases because the land is his property and cannot be rented without his permission. The basis of istihsan – the difference between building/planting and cultivation – is what has preceded. In al-Qunyah and al-Khassaf: If one leases waqf land to build or plant on it, then the lease period expires, the lessee may keep it with a rental at the like rate if there is no harm. Even if the beneficiary of the waqf refuses and demands removal, he does not have that right. This is the ruling of istihkar (long-term lease), and it applies to the author's absolute statement. In al-Muhit: And if... End quote. From here.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage covers two interrelated matn lines from Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding leasing land for building and planting. The first matn states that it is valid if the period is specified, analogous to leasing for cultivation. The commentary provides supporting examples and exceptions: sharing arrangements are invalid, and waqf property has special rules. The second matn addresses the expiry of the term: the lessee must remove structures and return the land empty. The commentary distinguishes this from cultivation, where crops are left until harvest due to a known end, and from usurpation, where removal is mandatory regardless. The key distinction is that building and planting have no natural limit, so immediate removal is required, whereas crops have a harvest season, allowing a grace period. The passage also discusses istihsan reasoning, comparing different scenarios to arrive at equitable rules. The final part mentions a special rule for waqf land allowing the lessee to retain buildings with rent under certain conditions (istihkar).

Key Terms
قلع (qal'): Uprooting or removing structures/trees from the land
استحكار (istihkar): A long-term lease allowing the lessee to keep improvements with rent payment

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best explains why a lessee who built on leased land must remove the building immediately after the lease ends, while a lessee who cultivated crops may leave them until harvest?
A) Because building is more harmful to the land than crops.
B) Because cultivation has a known end (harvest), while building/planting does not.
C) Because the lessor owns the building but not the crops.
D) Because the lease for building is always void anyway.

Key Takeaway
Leasing for building/planting is valid only with a known period; upon expiry, immediate removal is required because there is no natural end, unlike cultivation where crops may remain until harvest due to a known end and istihsan.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
beginner
6 min
Validity of Leasing Land for Building or Planting with Specified Duration
Explains the validity condition for leasing land for building/planting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leasing land for building or planting and explain why specifying the duration is essential for validity.

Core Idea
Leasing land for building or planting is valid only if the duration is specified, making the benefit known.

This lesson examines a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding Ijarah (leasing) of land for purposes other than agriculture—specifically for building or planting. The key condition is that the lease term must be clearly defined, otherwise the contract is invalid due to uncertainty (jahalah). Understanding this principle helps you appreciate how the Hanafi madhhab balances contractual freedom with the necessity of certainty in usufruct.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is leasing (ijarah) land for building (bina) or planting (ghars). The ruling is that it is permissible (jaiz) and valid (sahih).
The passage uses 'jaza' meaning it is permissible.
2
Locate the essential condition
The condition for validity is that the duration of the lease (al-mudda) must be specified (bayyin). Without a specified duration, the contract is invalid.
The text explicitly says 'in bayyana mudda' – if the duration is made clear.
3
Understand the proof (illa)
The reason for validity is that both the benefit (manfa'a) and the duration are known (ma'luma), eliminating uncertainty. This is the core principle of valid ijarah: the usufruct must be known.
The passage states 'li-anna al-manfa'a ma'luma wa al-mudda ma'luma'.
4
See the analogy to agriculture
The author analogizes this to leasing for agriculture, which is universally accepted as valid when the duration is known. This confirms that the same principle applies to building and planting.
"Ka-ma law ista'jaraha li-al-zira'a" – just as if he leased it for farming.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللبناء والغرس إن بين مدة يعني جاز استئجار الأرض للبناء والغرس بين مدة لأن المنفعة معلومة والمدة معلومة فتصح كما لو استأجرها للزراعة.
And for building and planting, if the duration is specified, meaning: it is permissible to lease land for building and planting for a specified duration, because the benefit is known and the time is known, so it is valid just as if he leased it for agriculture.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq explained by the commentator. It states that leasing land for building or planting is permissible if the duration of the lease is specified. The reason is that the benefit (the building or planting) and the duration are both known, making the contract valid. This is analogous to leasing land for agriculture, which is also valid when the duration is known. The underlying principle is that ignorance (jahalah) regarding the benefit or time would invalidate the contract, but specifying both removes that ignorance. Note that this ruling is specific to the Hanafi school; other schools may have different conditions.

Key Terms
غرس (ghars): Planting trees or vegetation in the leased land
بناء (bina'): Constructing a building on the leased land

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What makes leasing land for building or planting valid according to this passage?
A) The duration of the lease is specified
B) The lessee agrees to pay in advance
C) The landlord owns the building after the lease
D) The building is removable without harm

Key Takeaway
For a lease of land for building or planting to be valid in Hanafi law, the duration must be explicitly fixed, ensuring the usufruct is certain and free from jahalah.

Invalidity of Sharing Arrangement in Land Lease for Trees
Analyzing a case of invalid ijarah (fasad) when land is given for planting trees with a condition of sharing the land and trees

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a sharing arrangement in a land lease for trees is fasid (invalid) in Hanafi fiqh, identifying the two legal defects: unknown wage and prohibited qard of non-fungibles.

Core Idea
A lease with an unknown wage (share of output) is fasid; borrowing trees is invalid, turning the contract into a fasid qard.

This lesson examines a specific case from al-Muhit where a landowner gives his land to someone to plant trees on condition that both land and trees become shared equally. The Hanafi ruling declares this arrangement invalid, not as a valid partnership (musharakah) but as a fasid ijarah combined with a fasid qard. Understanding this case clarifies the limits of valid ijarah and the prohibition of lending non-fungible items.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and its condition
Read the case: a landowner gives his land to a planter to grow trees, with the condition that the land and the trees become jointly owned, half and half.
2
Analyze the defect in the wage
The wage (ujrah) is set as 'what comes out of the work' – a share of the output. Hanafi law requires the wage in ijarah to be known (ma'lum) at the time of contract. An unknown wage makes the contract fasid.
This is the first defect: unknown consideration.
3
Recognize the implied qard
By taking possession of the trees, the landowner becomes a borrower of the trees. However, trees are not fungible (mithli), so a qard of trees is invalid (fasid).
Second defect: loan of non-fungibles.
4
Understand the consequences
Despite invalidity, the trees become the property of the landowner because of the fasid qard (possession transfers ownership). The landowner must pay the value of the trees and the planter's wage for his labor.
The planter is not forced to uproot the trees – compensation replaces restitution.
5
Summarize the ruling
The arrangement is a fasid ijarah due to unknown wage, and it also contains a fasid qard. The landowner owns the trees but must compensate the planter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المحيط : دفع أرضه لرجل ليغرس أشجاراً على أن تكون الأرض والشجر بينهما نصفين لم يجز والشجر لرب الأرض وعليه قيمة الشجر وله أجر ما عمل ولا يؤمر بقلعه وهذه إجارة فاسدة لأنه جعل أجرة ما يخرج من العمل وعلى رب الأرض قيمة الأشجار لأنه صار مستقرضاً للأشجار منه وتقايضا لها حكماً واستقراض الأشجار لا يجوز فيكون قرضاً فاسداً فيوجب الملك إذا اتصل به القبض.
And in al-Muhit: A man gave his land to a person to plant trees on condition that the land and the trees be between them half and half – it is not permissible. The trees belong to the owner of the land, and he owes the value of the trees, and the planter has the wage for his work, and he is not ordered to uproot them. This is a fasad ijarah because he made the wage what comes out of the work. The owner of the land owes the value of the trees because he has become a borrower of the trees from him, and they have exchanged them in effect, and borrowing trees is not permissible, so it is a fasad qard, which necessitates ownership when possession is connected.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage presents a case from al-Muhit of a fasad (invalid) ijarah. A landowner gives his land to someone to plant trees on the condition that both the land and the trees become shared equally (half and half). The ruling is that this contract is invalid (lam yajuz). The trees are owned by the landowner, but he must pay the planter the value of the trees. The planter also receives the wage (ujr) for his work (i.e., the actual labor). The planter is not forced to uproot the trees because the landowner has effectively borrowed the trees and must compensate. The reasoning: the contract is a fasad ijarah because the 'wage' is set as a share of the output (what comes from the work), which is prohibited. Additionally, the landowner becomes a borrower of the trees (qard) since he takes possession of them, and borrowing trees is invalid (because trees are not fungible). Hence it becomes a fasad qard, which transfers ownership upon possession (qabd). This is a Hanafi ruling.

Key Terms
إجارة فاسدة (ijarah fasidah): An invalid lease contract due to a defect in the consideration or condition
قرض فاسد (qard fasid): An invalid loan because the object is not fungible or the transaction is not permissible

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case from al-Muhit, why does the landowner owe the value of the trees?
A) Because he agreed to buy them
B) Because he became a borrower of the trees through a fasad qard
C) Because the planter gifted them
D) Because the contract was valid

Key Takeaway
A lease with an unknown wage (share of output) and an implied loan of non-fungible items renders the contract fasid, requiring compensation.

Removal of Buildings and Trees at Lease End: Defaults and Exceptions
Explains the obligation to remove buildings and trees at lease end, and exceptions for crops and compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default ruling for removal of buildings and trees at the end of an ijarah and identify the exceptions based on istihsan.

Core Idea
Buildings and trees must be removed immediately at lease end, but crops may stay until harvest due to istihsan.

When a land lease expires, what happens to structures, trees, or crops placed by the lessee? The default Hanafi rule is that the lessee must remove them and return the land empty. However, the law recognises practical exceptions rooted in istihsan (juristic preference). This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind the default and the key exceptions, including crops, ghasb (usurpation), waqf land, and voluntary compensation by the lessor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
Find the basic rule: when the lease period ends, the lessee must uproot buildings and trees and return the land empty. Understand that this is wajib (obligatory) and immediate.
The text says 'because he must empty it and deliver it to its owner empty'.
2
Recognize the istihsan exception for crops
Contrast crops with buildings/trees. Crops have a known endpoint (harvest), so they are left until harvest with payment of ujr al-mithl (market rent). This is an istihsan departure from strict qiyas.
The key distinction is 'known end' (ghayah ma'lumah).
3
Distinguish from ghasb (usurpation)
Note that in cases of ghasb, even crops must be uprooted immediately because the initial act was oppressive. This shows the importance of the initial permission in ijarah.
The text says 'the initial act was oppression, and oppression must be removed, not confirmed.'
4
Note the waqf land exception
According to al-Qunyah and al-Khassaf, if the land is waqf, the lessee may keep buildings/trees with ujr al-mithl if no harm, even against the beneficiary's wish for removal.
This is an intra-Hanafi variation: the general ruling applies to private land, but waqf has a special rule.
5
Understand the compensation option
The lessor may choose to pay the value of the building/tree (when uprooted) and own it, or agree to let it remain. This is a voluntary arrangement to avoid waste.
This appears at the end of the passage from al-Muhit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن مضت المدة قلعهما وسلمها فارغة يعني إذا مضت مدة الإجارة قلع البناء والغرس وسلم الأرض إلى المؤجر فارغة لأنه يجب عليه تفريغها وتسليمها إلى صاحبها فارغة وذلك بقلعها في الحال لأنه ليس له غاية تعلم بخلاف ما إذا كانت للزراعة وانقضت المدة والزرع لم يدرك حيث يترك على حاله إلى الحصاد بأجر المثل لأن له غاية معلومة فأمكن مراعاة الجانبين وبخلاف ما إذا مات أحد المتعاقدين في المدة والزرع لم يدرك بحيث يترك بالأجرة على حاله إلى الحصاد وإن بطلت الإجارة فكان تركه بالمسمى وإبقاء العقد على ما كان أولى من النقض وإعادته، وبخلاف ما إذا غصب أرضاً وزرعها حيث يأمر بالقلع وإن كان له نهاية لأن ابتداء فعله ظلماً وقع والظلم يجب إعدامه لا تقريره والقياس أن يقلع في الأمور كلها لأن الأرض ملكه فلا تؤجر بغير إذنه. ووجه الاستحسان وهو الفرق بين البناء والغرس والزرع ما تقدم. وفي القنية والخصاف: استأجر أرضاً وقفاً ليبني فيها أو يغرس ثم مضت مدة الإجارة فللمستأجر أن يستبقيها بأجرة المثل إذا لم يكن في ذلك ضرر، ولو أبي الموقوف عليه إلا القلع فليس له ذلك علم حكم الاستحكار وهذا وارد على إطلاق المؤلف. وفي المحيط : وإذا إلا أن يغرم المؤجر قيمته مقلوعاً ويتملكه أو يرضى بتركه فيكون البناء والغرس لهذا والأرض لهذا والرطبة كالشجر والزرع يترك بأجرة المثل إلى أن يدرك
And when the period expires, he uproots them and returns it empty. He means: when the lease period expires, he uproots the building and the planting and delivers the land to the lessor empty because he must empty it and deliver it to its owner empty, and that by uprooting them immediately because there is no known end (for them). Contrary to the case when it is for agriculture and the period expires and the crop has not yet ripened; there it is left as it is until harvest with rent of the like because it has a known end, so it is possible to consider both sides. Also contrary to the case when one of the contracting parties dies during the period and the crop has not ripened; it is left with the named rent until harvest even if the ijarah is void, because leaving it with the named rent and preserving the contract as it was is better than dissolving and repeating. Also contrary to the case of usurping land and cultivating it; there he is ordered to uproot even if it has an end, because his initial act was oppression, and oppression must be removed, not confirmed. The qiyas is to uproot in all matters because the land is his property and is not leased without his permission. The istihsan and the distinction between building/planting and crops is what preceded. And in al-Qunyah and al-Khassaf: Someone leased waqf land to build or plant in it, then the lease period expired; the lessee may keep them with rent of the like if there is no harm. If the beneficiary refuses and demands removal, he does not have that right; he knows the ruling of istihkar, and this is against the absolute wording of the author. And in al-Muhit: Unless the lessor pays its value when uprooted and owns it, or he agrees to leave it, so the building and planting belong to this one and the land to that one.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage explains the default ruling when an ijarah for land with buildings or trees ends. The lessee must remove the structures and plants and return the land empty. However, agricultural crops are an exception: if the lease ends before harvest, the crops are left until harvest with payment of similar rent (ujr al-mithl) because the crop has a known endpoint (perfect ripeness). Similarly, if one party dies during the lease and crops are not yet ripe, the crops remain with the named rent until harvest. This is different from cases of usurpation (ghasb) where the usurper is forced to remove crops immediately. The underlying principle (istihsan) distinguishes between buildings/trees (which have no fixed growth endpoint) and crops (which do). The text also notes that waqf land may be treated differently: the lessee may retain buildings/trees with rent of the like if there is no harm, even against the waqf beneficiary's wishes. Finally, an exception is stated: the lessor may pay the value of the building/trees (if removal would damage the land) and own them, or the parties may agree to leave them.

Key Terms
قلع (qal'): Uprooting or removing buildings/trees from the land
أجر المثل (ujr al-mithl): The market rate rent for similar property or usufruct
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that allows departure from strict qiyas for a more equitable result

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the reason for allowing crops to remain after the lease period?
A) Crops are more valuable than buildings
B) Crops have a known endpoint (harvest)
C) Crops are owned by the lessee
D) The lessor cannot access the land

Key Takeaway
Buildings and trees must be removed immediately at lease end, but crops may stay until harvest due to istihsan; exceptions include waqf land and voluntary compensation.

Hiring Animals and Clothes: Specified or General Use
Main ruling on validity of hire with two methods of specifying benefit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the conditions for validity of hiring animals for riding/load and cloth for wearing, and distinguish between the two Hanafi interpretations of 'itlaq'.

Core Idea
A hire contract is valid if the benefit is known, whether by specification or generality.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a common practical issue: hiring an animal or cloth. The key is that the benefit must be known. The author explains that this can be achieved by either specifying exactly who will ride or wear the item, or by leaving it general with the phrase 'you may ride/wear whomever you wish.' However, later commentators differed on whether simply stating the purpose without naming a specific person counts as absolute. Let us examine the ruling and the two views.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Hiring animals for riding/load and cloth for wearing is permissible (sahih) if the benefit is known. The passage explicitly states this.
Benefit knowledge is the core condition.
2
Recognize the two methods to make benefit known
Specification (ta'yin) means designating a specific person; generalization (itlaq) means leaving it open. Both are valid.
3
Understand the two interpretations of 'itlaq'
Taj al-Shari'ah et al. interpret itlaq as explicit permission to choose whomever one wishes. Al-Nihayah et al. interpret it as merely stating the purpose without adding further specification.
Both interpretations are accepted in the Hanafi school.
4
Apply to examples
Hiring a horse for riding: if you say 'I hire this horse for riding,' that is itlaq under the second view; if you say 'I hire this horse for you to ride,' that is itlaq under the first view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والدابة للركوب والحمل والثوب للبس يعني يجوز استئجار هذه الأشياء لما ذكر إذا عين الراكب والحمل أو أطلق لأن لها منافع معلومة قيد بالركوب ليحترز عما إذا استأجرها كما تقدم، وباللبس ليحترز عما إذا استأجر الثوب ليزين به دكانه كما تقدم. وفي الذخيرة: استأجر دابة ليحمل عليها حنطة من موضع كذا إلى منزله وكان كلما رجع يركبها فعطبت الدابة قال أبو بكر الرازي: يضمن لأنه استأجرها للحمل دون الركوب فكان غاصباً بالركوب. وقال الفقيه أبو الليث : في الاستحسان لا يضمن لأن العادة جرت بين الناس بذلك فصار مأذوناً فيه. ثم شرع يبين أنها تارة تكون مطلقة وتارة تكون مقيدة. قال رحمه الله : (فإن أطلق أركب وألبس شاء) يعني إذا أطلق له الركوب واللبس جاز له أن يركب الدابة ويلبس الثوب من شاء، والمراد بالإطلاق أن يقول على أن تركب من تشاء وتلبس من تشاء .اهـ. كلام الشارح. وفسر الإطلاق بهذا تاج الشريعة وصاحب العناية والغاية، وفسر صاحب النهاية والكفاية ومعراج الدراية الإطلاق بأن يقول استأجرتها للركوب ولم يزد عليه أو اللبس ولم يزد عليه.
And the riding animal for riding and load, and the cloth for wearing. He means: it is permissible to hire these things for what was mentioned, if the rider and load are specified or left general, because they have known benefits. It is restricted by riding to avoid the case where he hires it as previously mentioned, and by wearing to avoid the case where he hires the cloth to adorn his shop as previously mentioned. And in al-Dhakhirah: Someone hired a riding animal to carry wheat from such-and-such a place to his house, and whenever he returned he would ride it, and the animal died. Abu Bakr al-Razi said: He is liable because he hired it for load, not riding, so he was a usurper by riding. Al-Faqih Abu al-Layth said by istihsan: He is not liable because custom among people is that, so he is considered permitted. Then he began to explain that sometimes it is absolute and sometimes restricted. He (the author) said: (If he leaves absolute, he rides and wears as he wishes). He means: if he leaves riding and wearing absolute, he may ride the animal and wear the cloth as he wishes, and the meaning of absoluteness is that he says: 'You are to ride whomever you wish and wear whomever you wish.' End of the commentator's words. Taj al-Shari'ah and the authors of al-Inayah and al-Ghayah explained absoluteness with this. The author of al-Nihayah, al-Kifayah, and Miraj al-Dirayah explained absoluteness as: he says 'I hired it for riding' and did not add anything, or for wearing and did not add anything.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage addresses hiring animals for riding/load and cloth for wearing. The ruling is that such contracts are valid if the use is either specified (e.g., a specific person to ride) or left general (e.g., 'you may ride whomever you wish'). The benefit must be known. The text restricts to riding and wearing to exclude hired items used for other purposes (like adorning a shop). There is a dispute: if the lessee uses the animal beyond the contract (e.g., rides it when hired only for carrying), Abu Bakr al-Razi says he becomes a usurper (ghasib) and is liable for damages. However, Abu al-Layth by istihsan says he is not liable if custom permits such use, because it becomes implied permission. The commentator then explains that the phrase 'if he leaves it absolute' means the lessor gives the lessee discretion to choose who rides or wears. Two interpretations of 'absolute' are given: (1) explicit permission to choose (Taj al-Shari'ah, etc.) or (2) simply stating the purpose without further specification (al-Nihayah, etc.).

Key Terms
إطلاق (itlaq): Leaving the use of the hired item unrestricted or unspecified
تقييد (taqyid): Restricting or specifying the use, e.g., appointing a specific rider or wearer
منفعة معلومة (manfa'ah ma'lumah): Known benefit that is the subject of the hire contract

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which condition must be met for a hire contract to be valid when hiring an animal for riding or a cloth for wearing?
A) The rider or wearer must be named specifically.
B) The benefit (manfa'ah) must be known, either by specification or generality.
C) The hire period must be fixed.
D) The owner must personally deliver the item.

Key Takeaway
A hire contract is valid if the benefit is known; 'itlaq' may mean explicit discretion or merely stating the purpose, both accepted in the Hanafi school.

Liability for Exceeding Specified Use: Qiyas vs Istihsan
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability for incidental use of a hired animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the two Hanafi views on liability when a lessee uses a hired animal beyond the contract terms, and evaluate the role of custom (urf) in overriding strict qiyas.

Core Idea
Custom can override strict qiyas: if riding an empty animal is customary, the lessee is not liable.

A practical problem: a man hires a donkey to carry his wheat, but on the return journey he rides it. The donkey dies. Is he liable? Two Hanafi scholars, Abu Bakr al-Razi and Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi, gave different answers. This lesson unpacks their arguments and shows how Hanafi fiqh balances textual reasoning (qiyas) with customary practice (istihsan).

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
The lessee hired the animal specifically to carry wheat, but also rode it on the return trip. The animal died.
2
Present Abu Bakr al-Razi's view and proof
He argues liability (daman) by qiyas: riding was not part of the contract, so the lessee became a usurper (ghasib) and is responsible for any damage.
Qiyas: the contract specifies load only; riding is a different use, thus a violation.
3
Present Abu al-Layth's view and proof
He argues no liability by istihsan: custom ('adah) among people permits riding the animal when returning empty, so it is considered implied permission (ma'dhun fih).
Istihsan: custom overrides strict qiyas because the contract is understood in light of customary practice.
4
Analyze the illa in qiyas
The effective cause (illa) for liability is using the animal in a manner not agreed upon. Abu al-Layth counters that custom makes the riding a permitted use.
5
Note the role of custom (urf)
Custom is a recognized source of law in Hanafi fiqh, especially in muamalat. It can clarify ambiguous terms or imply permissions.

Source Text

Three Types of Hiring (Ijara) and Their Rulings on Validity and Guarantee
Explanation of three hiring types and rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three types of hiring a riding animal or garment, state which types are fasid or sahih, and identify when the hirer becomes a guarantor due to ta'addi.

Core Idea
Uncertainty in hired use can be cured by actual use, making a fasid contract sahih by istihsan.

This passage from the Hanafi text Bahr al-Raiq breaks down the hiring ('ijara) of an animal or garment into three distinct scenarios. Each scenario has a different ruling on the contract's validity and the hirer's liability for damage or loss. Understanding these distinctions is essential for applying Hanafi law correctly in rental transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Types
The author presents three scenarios: (1) hiring without specifying a rider/wearer, (2) hiring with a condition allowing the hirer to use as he wishes, and (3) hiring with a specific rider/wearer named. Write them down as a mental taxonomy.
The first type has initial uncertainty (jahalah) about who will use the object.
2
Determine Initial Ruling for Each
The first type is ruled fasid (invalid) because riding and wearing differ vastly, creating excessive uncertainty. The second and third types are sahih (valid) because the condition removes the uncertainty.
Fasid in Hanafi law means defective but potentially curable; batil is void ab initio.
3
Analyze the Cure by Istihsan (First Type)
The first type becomes sahih after actual use (e.g., someone rides or wears) and the term passes. This is by istihsan: qiyas would keep it invalid, but istihsan considers the removal of uncertainty. The named rent becomes due.
No guarantee (daman) for damage if the object perishes because the hirer acted within permission.
4
Examine Guarantee and Transgression
In the third type, if the hirer deviates from the specified rider/wearer, he becomes a guarantor because he exceeds permission (ta'addi). The second type does not specify a person, so no transgression occurs if the hirer rides or lets another ride.
Rent and guarantee do not combine: if a guarantee is triggered, no rent is due, and vice versa.
5
Note the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
The author cites Abu al-Layth, who differs on hiring a garment for a specific place. If the hirer wears it elsewhere, Abu al-Layth says it's a change for the better, not a violation, so rent is due. The author disagrees.
This shows that even within the Hanafi school, there can be valid differences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
استئجار الدابة والثوب على ثلاثة أضرب : الأول أن يقول عند العقد استأجرتها للركوب أو للبس ولم يزد عليه. والثاني أن يزيد في قوله على أن أركب من أشاء وألبس من أشاء . والثالث أن يقول على أن أركب أنا أو فلان أو ألبس أنا أو فلان. ففي الوجه الأول يفسد العقد لأن الركوب واللبس مختلفان اختلافاً فاحشاً، فإن أركب شخصاً ومضت المدة تنقلب صحيحة ويجب المسمى استحساناً لأنه ارتفع الموجب للفساد وهو الجهالة ولا ضمان عليه إن هلكت لأنه غير متعد. وفي الوجه الثاني يصح العقد ويجب المسمى ويتعين أول من يركب، سواء كان المستأجر أو غيره لأنه تعين من الأصل فصار كأنه نص عليه ابتداء. وفي الثالث ليس له أن يتعداه لأن التعيين مفيد فإذا تعدى صار ضامناً وحكم الحمل حكم الركوب في جميع ما ذكرنا وفي قاضيخان استأجرت المرأة درعاً لتلبسه ثلاثة أيام إن كان الثوب بدله كان لها أن تلبسه في الأيام والليالي وإن كانت صيانة تلبسه في النهار وفي أول الليل وآخره وليس لها أن تلبسه كل الليل فإن لبسته كل الليل وباتت فيه حتى جاء النهار برئت من الضمان إن لم يتخرق .اهـ. وفي البقالي: استأجر دابة ليحمل عليها فحمل عليها رجلاً لا يضمن، ولو استأجر دابة ليطحن عليها وما بين مقدار ما يعمل به فإنه يجوز وله أن يعمل عليها مقدار ما تحمل. وفي المحيط : ينعقد فاسداً فإذا عمل عليها مقدار ما يحمل يعود جائزاً ويجب المسمى استحساناً، فظهر أن المشيئة في قوله ما شاء مقيدة بقدر حملها. وفي المحيط : استأجر ثوباً ليلبسه ليذهب إلى مكان كذا فلم يذهب إلى ذلك الموضع ولبسه في غير ذلك الموضع يكون مخالفاً ولا أجر عليه. وقال الفقيه أبو الليث : عندي أنه غير مخالف ويجب الأجر لأن هذا خلاف إلى خير وليس هذا كمن استأجر دابة ليذهب إلى موضع كذا فركبها في المصر في حوائجه فهو مخالف لأن الدابة لا يجوز إيجارها إلا إذا بين المكان وفي الثوب لا يحتاج إلى بيان المكان .اهـ. وفي الخلاصة : وإذا تكارى قوم مشاة ابلاً على أن المكاري يحمل عليها من مرض منهم أو من أغمي عليه منهم فهذا فاسد. قال رحمه الله : (وإن قيد براكب ولابس مخالف ضمن) يعني إذا عطبت لأن التقييد مقيد فتعين فإذا خالف صار ضامناً بالتعدي لأن الناس يتفاوتون في الركوب واللبس ولا أجر عليه لأن الأجر والضمان لا يجتمعان وكذا الأجرة عليه إن سلم بخلاف ما إذا استأجر حانوتاً وأقعد فيه قصاراً أو حداداً حيث يجب الأجر لأنه لما سلم تبين أنه لم يخالف؛ كذا في غاية البيان. واستفيد من كلامه أنه إذا قيد ليس له الإجارة والإعارة كما إذا وليس له الإيداع عمم في الأول ولا ضرورة دون الثاني ؛ كذا في فصول العمادي. كما إذا عمي الحمار في الطريق.
Hiring an animal and a garment are of three types: First, that he says at the contract 'I hired it for riding' or 'for wearing' and does not add anything. Second, that he adds in his statement 'on condition that I ride whom I wish' or 'wear what I wish'. Third, that he says 'on condition that I ride or so-and-so' or 'that I wear or so-and-so'. In the first case, the contract is invalid because riding and wearing differ vastly. If he then rides a person and the term passes, it becomes valid and the named rent is due istihsanan because the cause of invalidity—ignorance—has been removed, and there is no guarantee if it perishes because he is not transgressing. In the second case, the contract is valid and the named rent is due, and the first rider is determined, whether the hirer or another, because it was determined from the outset, so it is as if he specified it initially. In the third, he may not go beyond it because specification is beneficial; if he does, he becomes guarantor. The ruling of loading is like the ruling of riding in all we have mentioned. In Qadikhan: A woman hires a garment to wear for three days; if the garment is not valuable, she may wear it day and night; if it is valuable, she wears it in the daytime and at the beginning and end of the night, and she may not wear it all night; if she wears it all night and sleeps in it until morning, she is free from guarantee if it does not tear. End quote. In al-Baqqali: One hires a donkey to load on it, then loads a man on it—he does not guarantee. And if he hires a donkey to grind on it—whatever is within the capacity of its work, it is permissible and he may work on it to the extent of what it can carry. In al-Muhit: It is contracted as invalid; then when he works on it to the extent of what it can carry, it returns to being valid and the named rent is due istihsanan. So it becomes clear that the discretion in his statement 'what I wish' is restricted by its carrying capacity. In al-Muhit: One hires a garment to wear to go to a certain place, then does not go to that place and wears it in another place—he is violator and there is no rent due. Abu al-Layth said: In my view he is not a violator and rent is due because this is a change for the better; it is not like one who hires a donkey to go to a certain place and rides it in the city for his needs—he is a violator because the donkey cannot be hired unless the place is specified, whereas the garment does not require specifying the place. End quote. In al-Khulasa: If a group of pedestrians hire camels on condition that the hirer carries on them any who fall sick or faint, this is invalid. He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And if restricted to a specific rider and wearer and violates, he is a guarantor' meaning if it is destroyed, because the restriction is binding, so it becomes specific; if he violates, he becomes a guarantor due to transgression because people vary in riding and wearing, and there is no rent for him because rent and guarantee do not combine; likewise, the rent is due on him if it is delivered, unlike when one hires a shop and places a fuller or blacksmith in it, where rent is due because when it is delivered it becomes clear that he did not violate; as in Ghayat al-Bayan. And it is understood from his statement that if restricted, he may not lease out or lend, nor deposit; it is general in the first and no necessity for the second; as in Fusul al-Imadi. Just as if the donkey goes blind on the road.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory expansion of rulings on hiring animals and garments. The author divides hiring into three distinct types and discusses each. The first type is hiring without specifying a rider or wearer, which renders the contract fasid (invalid) due to gharar (uncertainty). However, if the hirer actually uses the object by letting another person ride or wear it, the contract becomes sahih (valid) by istihsan, as the cause of invalidity disappears. The second type includes a condition that the hirer may ride or wear as he wishes, which is valid because the specification is broad yet known to the parties. The first person to use becomes the intended user. The third type specifies a particular person, which restricts use; violation makes the hirer a guarantor. The author then extrapolates to loading, equating it to riding. Additional rulings from Qadikhan, al-Baqqali, and al-Muhit illustrate practical applications: a woman hiring a garment, a donkey hired for grinding, and the restriction of 'as I wish' to the animal's capacity. The debate between Abu al-Layth and the author regarding hiring a garment for a specific location shows an intra-Hanafi difference. The passage concludes with the matn statement on restriction and guarantee, emphasizing that if a specific rider or wearer is stipulated, any deviation makes the hirer a guarantor, and no rent is due because rent and guarantee are mutually exclusive. Exceptions are noted, such as hiring a shop and changing the trade, where no violation occurs if the use is not harmful.

Key Terms
فساد العقد (fasad al-'aqd): Invalidity of contract due to fundamental defect such as uncertainty (jahalah) in the subject matter.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that sets aside qiyas (analogy) for a more equitable ruling based on consideration of public interest or custom.
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss or destruction of the hired object due to transgression (ta'addi).
تعدي (ta'addi): Transgression or exceeding the limits of permission granted in the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the first type of hiring (unspecified rider), when does the contract become valid?
A) Immediately at the time of contract.
B) Only if the hirer himself rides.
C) After actual use by someone and the term passes.
D) Never; it remains fasid.

Key Takeaway
Hiring contracts: specify the user or allow broad discretion; if unspecified, the contract becomes valid by actual use (istihsan); deviation from specification triggers guarantee.

When Restrictions in Ijarah Are Void: The Criterion of Variation
Explanation of when restriction matters and when it is void based on whether usage varies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a restriction on use in ijarah is void when the use does not vary among users, and you will be able to distinguish between the treatment of a house and a tent based on the intra-Hanafi difference.

Core Idea
A restriction on use in ijarah is void if the use does not vary — uniformity nullifies the condition.

In Hanafi ijarah law, not every contractual restriction is binding. The school carefully examines whether the restricted use actually differs from person to person. If the use is uniform, like dwelling in a house, then a condition limiting it to a specific person is meaningless and therefore void. This lesson unpacks that principle and explores a key difference of opinion regarding tents, where the variation in setup creates a dispute between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The passage discusses ijarah (hire) and whether a restriction (taqyid) on use is valid. The ruling: if the use does not vary among users, the restriction is void (batal).
The act is the stipulation of a condition in the ijarah contract.
2
Understand the criterion of variation
The key criterion is whether the use in question differs with the user (yakhtalif bi al-musta'mil). If it does not, the restriction serves no purpose and is ignored.
Example: dwelling in a house is essentially the same for all people, so a restriction to 'only one person may dwell' is void.
3
Apply to the example of a house
The text explicitly gives the example: if the lessor stipulates that only a specific person may dwell in a house, the hirer may let another person dwell. The restriction is null.
This applies to any use that is uniform, like storage of similar goods.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on tents
For a tent (fustat), there is a difference: Muhammad considers it like a house (restriction void), while Abu Yusuf compares it to clothing (restriction effective) because setting up a tent varies among people (nusub, awtad, location).
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf): under Muhammad, the hirer may sublet; under Abu Yusuf, he may not.
5
Note the exception for harmful uses
The text also mentions that if the use damages the building (e.g., blacksmith, fuller, miller), the restriction is effective even if the use is uniform, because of the harm.
This is an exception to the general rule, preserving the lessor's right to protect the asset.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ومثله ما يختلف بالمستعمل) يعني يضمن مثله في كل شيء يختلف باختلاف المستعمل إذا كان مقيداً وخالف لما ذكرنا من المعنى. قال رحمه الله: (وفيما لا يختلف بطل تقييده كما لو شرط سكنى واحد له أن يسكن غيره) يعني فيما لا يختلف باختلاف المستعمل كالدور للسكنى لا يعتبر تقييده حتى إذا شرط سكنى واحد له أن يسكن غيره لأن التقييد لا يفيد لعدم التفاوت وما يضر بالبناء كالحداد والقصار والطحان خارج كما مر . والفسطاط كالدار عند محمد وعند أبي يوسف مثل اللبس لاختلاف الناس في نصبه وضرب أوتاده واختيار مكانه.
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And similarly, that which varies with the user's means he is guarantor for the like in everything that varies with the user if it is restricted and he violates, due to the meaning we mentioned. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And in that which does not vary, his restriction is void, as if he stipulates dwelling of one, he may let another dwell' meaning in what does not vary with the user, like houses for dwelling, his restriction is not considered, to the extent that if he stipulated dwelling of one, he may let another dwell, because the restriction is useless due to lack of variation. And that which damages the building, like the blacksmith, fuller, and miller, is excluded as previously mentioned. And the tent is like the house according to Muhammad, and according to Abu Yusuf it is like wearing, due to people's variation in setting it up, striking its pegs, and choosing its location.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage presents two matn statements and their commentary. The first matn states that the ruling of guarantee for violation applies to anything that varies with the user. For example, if someone hires a shop and is restricted to a certain trade, and then uses it for a different trade that varies in impact, he is guarantor. The second matn states that if the use does not vary, the restriction is void. A clear example is a house for dwelling: people do not differ in the essence of dwelling, so stipulating 'only one person may dwell' is meaningless; the hirer can let others dwell. However, if the use harms the building, like blacksmithing, the restriction is effective. The commentary also notes a difference between Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding tents: Muhammad considers a tent like a house (restriction void), while Abu Yusuf compares it to clothing (restriction effective) because setting up a tent varies among people.

Key Terms
تقييد (taqyid): Restriction imposed by the lessor on how the hired object is used
فسطاط (fustat): A tent or pavilion

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person hires a house with the stipulation that only he may dwell, and then allows his friend to stay, what is the ruling?
A) He is a violator and owes guarantee.
B) He is not a violator and the restriction is void.
C) The contract becomes invalid.
D) He must pay extra rent.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi ijarah, a restriction on use is only effective if the use varies among users or causes harm to the property; otherwise, the condition is void and the hirer may use the object freely.

Carrying Alternative Loads on a Hired Animal: The Rule and Its Istihsan Refinement
Ruling on carrying similar or lighter loads when a specific type and quantity are stipulated

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the istihsan-based ruling that carrying a lighter or equivalent load of a different type is permissible without guarantee, and distinguish it from the stricter qiyas position.

Core Idea
Consent to a load implies consent to its like or lighter, but harm defines what is lighter.

In hiring an animal for a specified load, the law permits carrying a load of the same or lesser harm. But what does 'lesser harm' mean? This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq examines a case where a hirer carries barley instead of wheat of equal weight. While strict analogy (qiyas) would impose liability, the Hanafi school uses juristic preference (istihsan) to exempt the hirer because barley spreads out, causing less pressure on the animal. This lesson explores the reasoning and the preferred fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling from the matn
The matn states that if type and quantity are specified, the hirer may carry a load that is its like or lighter, but not more harmful. Understand the general permission.
The matn gives examples: barley, sesame are lighter; salt is harmful.
2
Analyze the qiyas argument for guarantee
According to al-Nihaya, carrying barley of equal weight triggers guarantee because barley occupies more space, similar to carrying waterskin or firewood. This is the qiyas position.
The analogy is based on the harm of occupying space.
3
Examine the istihsan objection
Shaykh al-Islam argues that barley, despite taking more space, spreads out and is actually lighter on the animal. Therefore, no guarantee is needed. This is istihsan overriding qiyas.
The principle: actual benefit and custom inform the ruling.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
The preferred view (fatwa of al-Sadr al-Shahid) is that the hirer is not liable for carrying equal-weight barley. This is the operative ruling.
This reflects the Hanafi reliance on istihsan in muamalat.
5
Apply the final principle to other loads
Apply the rule to other examples: iron (concentrated, harmful → guarantee), cotton (spreads, light → no guarantee). The key is the nature of harm, not just weight.
The concluding principle: permission for one does not imply permission for another if harm differs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وإن سمى نوعاً وقدراً ككر بر له حمل مثله وأخف لا أضر كالملح) يعنى لو سمى النوع والقدر فله أن يحمل على الدابة ما هو مثله وأخف كما لو استأجر ليحمل هذه الحنطة وهي قدر معلوم فحمل مثل قدرها وما هو أخف منه كالشعير والسمسم، وليس له أن يحمل عليها ما هو أضر منه كالملح لأن الرضا بالشيء يكون رضا بما هو مثله أو دونه عادة بما هو أضر منه لأنه لا فائدة في إجازة كر حنطة ومنع كر شعير بل الشعير أخف منه فكان أولى بالجواز حتى لو سمى الحنطة فحمل عليها من مثله وزناً ضمن لأن الشعير يأخذ من ظهر الدابة أكثر ما تأخذ الحنطة فصار كما لو حمل عليها قربة ماء أو حطب؛ كذا في النهاية. وقال شيخ الإسلام في شرحه : لا يضمن استحساناً. وقال: وهو الأصح لأن ضرر الشعير عند استوائهما في الوزن أخف من ضرر الحنطة لأنه يأخذ من ظهر الدابة أكثر مما تأخذ الحنطة فكان أخف عليها بالانبساط، وبه كان يفتي الصدر الشهيد، ولو حمل عليها مثل وزنه حديداً أو ملحاً يضمن لأنه يجتمع في مكان واحد من ظهر الدابة فيضر بها أكثر، وكذا لا يضمن إذا حمل عليها مثل وزنها قطناً لأنه يأخذ من ظهر الدابة أكثر وفيه حرارة، وما ذكرناه وجه الاستحسان والقياس أنه يضمن في الشعير ونحوه . والحاصل أن الشيئين متى كان في كل واحد منهما ضرر فوق ضرر الآخر من وجه لا يستفاد من الإذن في أحدهما الإذن في الآخر وإن كان هو أخف ضرراً من وجه آخر.
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And if he specifies type and quantity, like a load of wheat, he may carry its like and lighter, not more harmful, like salt' meaning if he specifies type and quantity, he may carry on the animal what is its like and lighter, as if he hires to carry this wheat of known quantity, then carries its like in quantity and what is lighter than it, like barley and sesame; and he may not carry on it what is more harmful, like salt, because consent to a thing is consent to its like or what is normally below it; as for what is more harmful, there is no benefit in allowing a load of wheat and preventing a load of barley; rather barley is lighter, so it is more deserving of permissibility. Even if he specified wheat and carried its like in weight, he is guarantor because barley takes up more of the animal's back than wheat, so it becomes as if he carried a waterskin or firewood; as in al-Nihaya. And Shaykh al-Islam said in his commentary: he does not guarantee istihsanan, and it is the most correct because the harm of barley when equal in weight is lighter than the harm of wheat because it takes up more of the animal's back, so it is lighter on it by spreading; and al-Sadr al-Shahid used to give fatwa accordingly. And if he carried its like in weight, iron or salt, he is guarantor because it concentrates in one place on the animal's back and harms it more; likewise, he does not guarantee if he carried its like in weight, cotton, because it takes up more of the animal's back and has heat. And what we mentioned is the face of istihsan, while by qiyas he would guarantee for barley and the like. The conclusion is that whenever two things each have harm exceeding the other in some respect, permission for one does not imply permission for the other, even if the one is less harmful in another respect.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage expands on the matn regarding specifying type and quantity. The general ruling is that if the hirer specifies a load (e.g., wheat of a certain quantity), he may carry an equal or lighter load (e.g., barley or sesame), but not a heavier or more harmful one (e.g., salt). The commentary then presents a nuanced discussion. According to al-Nihaya, if he carries barley of equal weight to wheat, he is guarantor because barley occupies more space on the animal's back, causing harm similar to carrying a waterskin. However, Shaykh al-Islam (a later authority) holds that he does not guarantee istihsanan because barley, despite taking more space, is actually lighter on the animal due to spreading, and this is the preferred view followed by al-Sadr al-Shahid. The author explains that the difference arises from two perspectives: qiyas would imply guarantee for any different load, but istihsan considers the actual harm. The concluding principle is that permission for one type does not automatically permit another if there is a difference in harm, even if from one perspective it seems less harmful.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference used here to override qiyas in favor of a more practical ruling based on actual harm
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning that would require guarantee for any deviation in load

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person hires a donkey to carry a specified load of wheat, and then carries an equal weight of barley, what is the relied-upon ruling?
A) He is guarantor by qiyas.
B) He is not guarantor by istihsan.
C) He must pay additional rent.
D) The contract becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prioritizes actual harm over strict analogy: a different load of equal weight may be permissible if it is less harmful, relying on istihsan.

The Validity of Hiring Animals without Specification: The Principle of Jahalat al-Alah
Rulings on hiring animals without specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hiring named but unspecified animals for transport and explain the principle of jahalat al-alah.

Core Idea
Ignorance of the tool does not invalidate a contract when the service is well-defined on liability.

This lesson examines a key ruling from Imam Muhammad's al-Asl regarding the ijarah of camels for travel to Mecca. The author clarifies that the contract is valid despite the ambiguity of the specific animal because the service is on the hirer's liability. This introduces the Hanafi principle that ignorance of the instrument (jahalat al-alah) does not cause invalidity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and ambiguity
The case involves hiring 'named camels' without specifying which ones. Determine the type of ambiguity.
2
Understand 'service on liability'
The service (carriage) is in the hirer's liability (dhimmah), making the animals mere tools. This is key to validity.
Liabilities are known; tools are incidental.
3
Learn jahalat al-alah principle
Ignorance of the tool (e.g., which camel) does not invalidate, analogous to hiring a tailor without specifying his scissors.
4
Contrast with hiring slave for service
The text notes that hiring a slave without specification is invalid, highlighting the difference between tool and subject matter.
5
Conclude with the adopted fatwa
Al-Sadr al-Shahid affirms fatwa of permissibility without interpretation, establishing the school's position.

وفي الأصل : إذا تكارى من رجلا إبلاً مسماة بغير عينها إلى مكة فالإجارة جائزة . قال شيخ الإسلام: ليس تفسير المسألة ما ذكرنا بل تفسيرها استأجر المكاري على الحمل فالمقصود عليه الحمل في ذمة المكاري وأنه معلوم والإبل آلة وجهالة الآلة لا توجب فساد الإجارة كما في الخياط والقصار وما أشبهة. واستدل على تفسير المسألة بما ذكر أنه لو استأجر عبداً للخدمة لا بعينه لا يجوز . قال الصدر الشهيد ونحن نفتي بالجواز كما ذكر في الكتاب من غير تأويل. وفي الذخيرة : استأجر دابة إلى كذا ودفع له الدابة لا يجبر رب الدابة أن يرسل غلامه معها. قال محمد: يؤمر بأن يرسل غلامه معها . قال شيخ الإسلام : إن شاء لأنه لا يجبر عليه. وفي الصيرفية : استأجر دابة بعينها للحمل فحمل المكاري على غيرها لا يستحق الأجرة ويكون متبرعاً. وفي الفتاوى : تکارى دابة إلى موضع معلوم بأربعة دراهم على أن يرجع في يومه فلم يرجع إلى خمسة أيام قال : يجب در همان أجرة الذهاب لأنه مخالف في الرجوع. ولو استأجر دابة إلى مكة
In al-Asl: If a man hires from another named camels without specifying their identity to go to Mecca, the ijarah is permissible. Shaykh al-Islam said: The interpretation of the issue is not what we mentioned; rather its interpretation is that the hirer hires for carrying, so the obligation is on the hirer's liability, and that is known, and the camels are tools; ignorance of the tool does not invalidate the ijarah, just like the tailor and fuller and the like. He argued for this interpretation by what was mentioned: if he hires a slave for service without specification, it is not permissible. Al-Sadr al-Shahid said: We give fatwa of permissibility as mentioned in the book without interpretation. In al-Dhakhira: He hires a donkey to such-and-such and hands over the donkey; the owner of the donkey is not compelled to send his servant with it. Muhammad said: He is ordered to send his servant with it. Shaykh al-Islam said: He may if he wishes, because he is not compelled. In al-Sayrafiyya: He hires a specific donkey for loading, then the hirer loads on another; he does not deserve rent and is a volunteer. In al-Fatawa: He hires a donkey to a known place for four dirhams on condition that he returns on the same day, and he does not return for five days; it is said: he owes two dirhams for the going because he violated in the return. And if he hires a donkey to Mecca...
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage collects several independent rulings from different sources within the Hanafi school. The first ruling from al-Asl (by Imam Muhammad) states that hiring named camels without specifying which ones for a trip to Mecca is valid. Shaykh al-Islam explains that this is because the object is the carriage in the hirer's liability, and the camels are merely tools; ignorance of the tool does not cause invalidity, analogous to hiring a tailor without specifying his tools. Al-Sadr al-Shahid affirms the fatwa of permissibility. The second ruling from al-Dhakhira addresses whether the owner of a hired donkey must send his servant with it; the preferred view is that he is not compelled. The third ruling from al-Sayrafiyya states that if a specific animal is hired and the hirer uses a different one, he does not deserve rent. The fourth from al-Fatawa discusses a case where the hirer violates a condition about returning the same day; he owes additional rent for the going trip. The text cuts off mid-sentence on the next case.

Key Terms
المكاري (al-mukari): The person who hires out an animal for transport
جهالة الآلة (jahalat al-alah): Ignorance of the specific tool or instrument used in the service contract

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage from al-Asl, what is the ruling on hiring named camels without specifying their identity for a trip to Mecca?
A) The contract is invalid due to uncertainty.
B) The contract is permissible because the service is on liability.
C) The contract is valid only if the camels are physically present.
D) The contract requires additional payment.

Key Takeaway
Ignorance of the specific tool (jahalat al-alah) does not invalidate a service contract when the service is well-defined on liability.

The Lessor's Obligation to Send a Servant with the Hired Animal
Dispute on sending servant with hired donkey

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on whether a lessor must provide a servant with the hired animal.

Core Idea
The lessor is not compelled to send a servant; the permissibility depends on the contract's terms.

This lesson examines a dispute within the Hanafi school regarding whether the owner of a hired donkey must also send a servant with it. From al-Dhakhira, we see Imam Muhammad's view that he is ordered to do so, while Shaykh al-Islam holds he is not compelled. The analysis determines the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the dispute
A man hires a specific donkey; the owner hands over the donkey. The question: must the owner also send a servant?
2
Note Imam Muhammad's view
Imam Muhammad said the owner is ordered (yu'mar) to send a servant with the donkey.
3
Note Shaykh al-Islam's view
Shaykh al-Islam said the owner may send a servant if he wishes, because he is not compelled (yujbar). This implies the 'order' is moral and not legally enforceable.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
In this passage, Shaykh al-Islam's view is presented as the relied-upon position, as he clarifies that there is no compulsion.
5
Apply to similar scenarios
If the contract does not explicitly require a servant, the owner is not obligated to provide one.

Consequences of Breach of Conditions and Unauthorized Use of Hired Animals
Rulings on breach of contract and unauthorized use

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the rent owed when a hirer breaches a condition or uses an unauthorized animal.

Core Idea
Breach of condition or unauthorized substitution results in loss of rent or additional compensation.

This lesson examines two rulings from al-Sayrafiyya and al-Fatawa that address misuse of hired animals. In the first, if the hirer loads a different animal than the one specified, he becomes a volunteer and deserves no rent. In the second, if the hirer fails to return on the agreed day, he owes extra rent for the going trip due to violation of condition.

Guided Path
1
Case 1: Unauthorized substitution
The hirer hires a specific donkey for loading, but loads a different donkey. The owner does not deserve rent and is considered a volunteer.
2
Understand the reason: 'mutabarri'
Because the owner did not consent to the different animal; his act is gratuitous.
3
Case 2: Breach of return time
Hirer agrees to return the same day but returns after five days. He owes two dirhams for the going trip (the agreed rent was four dirhams for return trip as well?).
4
Extract the principle
Violating a condition (mukhalifah) changes the legal status; the owner is entitled to rent for the mitigated service.
5
Apply to modern scenarios
Similar logic applies to rental contracts where conditions are breached.
