intermediate
15 min
Liability for Adding an Extra Rider (Irdaf)
Explains the ruling when a hirer adds an extra rider and the animal perishes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability when an extra rider (irdaf) is added to a hired animal, explain the qiyas-based proof from injury law, and apply the ruling to various scenarios regarding capacity and type of extra rider.

Core Idea
When two riders cause the animal's death, liability is divided by number, not weight, by analogy with injury law.

This lesson unpacks a key Hanafi ruling from the chapter of Ijarah: what happens when a hirer adds an unauthorized extra rider and the animal perishes? The ruling is derived by qiyas (analogy) to the law of injuries, where multiple participants share liability equally. We will walk through the ruling, its proof, and several practical branches.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Identify the action (the hirer adds an extra rider without permission) and the consequence (the animal perishes). Then state the ruling: the hirer guarantees half the value if the animal could carry two riders, and the full value if it could not.
The ruling is from the matn: 'wa in 'atibat bil-irdaf damina al-nisf'.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is qiyas to the chapter of injuries (jinaayah). In jinaayah, when multiple persons cause an injury, liability is divided equally by number, not by the degree of contribution. The same logic applies here because both are cases of multiple parties causing harm.
The text explicitly says: 'ka al-jinaayah fi bab al-jinaayah'.
3
Explain the wajh al-dalalah (legal link)
The effective cause (illah) is that the harm is caused by multiple agents and the precise contribution of each cannot be measured. In jinaayah, it is divided by number; here too, the animal's destruction is caused by two riders, so they share liability equally regardless of weight.
The Hanafi position also adduces that humans are not weighed, so number is the only practical basis.
4
Consider the sub-rules and exceptions
The ruling changes if the animal cannot carry two (then full guarantee), if the extra rider is a child who cannot hold himself (then guarantee by weight), or if the extra rider is seated in the saddle (then he is a usurper and the hirer is not liable). Also, if the animal perishes after reaching the destination, full hire is due in addition to half value.
These are detailed in the commentary from al-Kafi, al-Muhit, etc.
5
Apply to a concrete scenario
Given a scenario with specific facts (capacity, type of extra rider, time of death), determine the guarantee amount and whether full hire is owed. Use the steps above.
Practice applying the rule to ensure understanding of the conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإجارة باب ما يجوز من الإجارة وما يكون خلافاً فيها
كالملح[؟] وإن عطبت بالأرداف ضمن النصف وبالزيادة على الحمل المسمى ما زاد
أو من أعيا فهو على الذهاب، وفي الغاية على الذهاب والرجوع وفي فتاوى : هو استأجر دابة ليحمل عليها مائة من الحنطة فمرضت فلم تطق إلا خمسين فحمل عليها هل يرجع على المكاري بحصة ذلك؟ قال القاضي بديع الدين : لا يرجع لأنه رضي بذلك. وفي جامع الفتاوى : استأجر دابة يوماً وانتفع بها فأمسكها وقد ورم بطنها أو اعتلت فتركت في الدار الذي هو فيما فماتت غرم. وفي العتابية: تكارى قوم مشاة إبلاً على أن المكاري يحمل من مرض منهم منهم فالإجارة فاسدة وفي الأصل ولو شرطوا عليه أن يركب واحد منهم فيه ثم يركب الآخر وهكذا فذلك جائز. وفي الخلاصة : تكارى على دخول عشرين يوماً إلى موضع كذا فما دخل إلا في خمسة وعشرين يوماً قال : يحط عنه من الأجرة بحساب ذلك ويستقيم على قول أبي يوسف ومحمد اهـ. وفي الخلاصة : رجل اكترى إبلاً للحج ثم اختلفوا في وقت الخروج فالقول في ذلك قول من يريد الخروج في الوقت المعروف للخروج اهـ. وفي المحيط : تكارى دابة بغير عينها إلى موضع كذا لم يجز لأن هذا عقد واحد والمعقود عليه في كل مجهول جهالة تؤدي إلى النزاع استأجر دابة إلى موضع كذا وضعفت قبل الوصول فعليه أن يأتي بغيرها لأن العقد لا ينفسخ في هذه الحالة، وإن كانت بعينها فليس عليه أن يأتي بغيرها فيفسخ العقد، ولو استأجر رجل دابتين بعشرة صفقة واحدة ليحمل عليها عشرين فقيزاً فحمل على كل دابة عشرة يقسم الأجر على أجر مثل كل دابة اهـ.
قال رحمه الله : (وإن عطبت بالأرداف ضمن النصف) يعني إذا استأجر دابة فأردف عليها غیره ضمن نصف القيمة ولا يعتبر بالثقل لأن الدابة يعقرها الراكب الخفيف ويخف عليها ركوب الثقيل لعلمه بالفروسية، ولأن الآدمي غير موزون فلا يمكن معرفته بالوزن فيتعلق الحكم بالعدد كالجناية في باب الجناية هذا إذا كانت الدابة تطيق حمل الأثنين، وإن كانت لا تطيق ضمن جميع قيمتها ؛ ذكره في الكافي . قالوا هذا إذا كان الرديف يستمسك بنفسه، وإن كان صغيراً لا يستمسك بنفسه يضمن بقدر ثقله . قال في النهاية : قيد بالرديف احترازاً عما إذا حمله على عاتقه فإنه يضمن جميع القيمة لأن ثقله مع الذي حمله يجتمعان في مكان واحد فيكون أشق على الدابة. وقال الحدادي : الرديف مثال وليس بقيد حتى لو جعل المستأجر نفسه رديفاً وغيره أصيلاً فالحكم واحد وفي غاية البيان : قيد بكونه رديفاً لأنه لو أقعد الأجنبي في السرج صار غاصباً ولم يجب عليه شيء من الأجرة قال قاضيخان: استأجر دابة ليركبها إلى موضع كذا فحمل عليها صبياً صغيراً فعطبت ضمن قيمتها كما لو حمل عليها حملاً. وأطلق في ضمان النصف فشمل ما إذا هلكت قبل الوصول أو بعده قال : وعليه جميع الأجرة إذا هلكت بعدما بلغ مقصده ونصف القيمة إذا هلكت قبله. وفي المحيط : إذا عطبت بعد البلوغ من الركوب فعليه الأجر كاملاً ونصف القيمة كان الرديف أخف أو أثقل، أما الأجرة فلأنه استوفى المعقود عليه، وأما الضمان فلأن التلف حصل بركوبهما ولم يبين من عليه الضمان فالمالك بالخيار إن شاء ضمن الرديف وإن شاء ضمن المستأجر ، فإن ضمن المستأجر لا يرجع بما ضمن، وإن ضمن الرديف يرجع إن كان مستأجراً وإلا فلا. وفي الخانية فإذا أراد صاحب الدابة أن يضمن الرديف نصف القيمة كان له ذلك. وفي التتارخانية : استأجر دابة ليحمل عليها عشرة أقفزة فأجرها من غيره فحمل عليها عشرين فتلفت يخير المالك في التضمين إن شاء ضمن الثاني ويرجع على الأول لأنه غره، وإن ضمن الأول لا يرجع على الثاني .اهـ. وأقول : ينبغي أن يفصل بأنه إن علم أنه مستأجر لما ذكر ينبغي أن لا يرجع على الأول، وإن علم أنه مالك أو لم يعلم ينبغي أن يرجع وأطلق المؤلف في الإرداف فشمل ما إذا أردف في كل المدة أو بعضها. وفي المحيط : استأجر دابة ذاهباً وراجعاً بعلفها فركبها ذاهباً وحمل عليها متاعاً وأردف آخر راجعاً فعليه أجرة مثلها في الذهاب لأن الأجارة وقعت فاسدة لجهالة العلف، وفي الرجوع ركبها اثنان فهلكت فعليه نصف القيمة ولما زاد من الحمل ويعرف ذلك بالرجوع إلى أهل الخبرة. وهذا إذا لم يركب على الحمل، إما إذا ركب عليه يضمن جميع قيمتها لأنه يحتمل ثقله وثقل الحمل عليها. ولو استأجر محمل الولد معها فتلفت ضمن بقدر الولد وكذا لو ولدت الناقة فحمل ولدها عليها. وقيد بالعطب لأنها لو سلمت يجب عليه الأجر تماماً .
Book of Ijarah, Chapter on what is permissible in Ijarah and what is disputed. Like salt[?] and if it perishes due to an extra rider, he guarantees half, and for exceeding the named load, he guarantees the excess. Or if it becomes exhausted, it is on the going, and in al-Ghayah on going and returning. And in Fatawa: He hired a donkey to carry 100 measures of wheat, it became ill and could only carry 50, so he loaded it – can he recover the portion from the carrier? Qadi Badī‘ al-Dīn said: No, because he consented. In Jami‘ al-Fatawa: He hired a donkey for a day and used it, then he detained it, its belly swelled or it became sick, so he left it in the house and it died – he pays. In al-‘Utābiyyah: A group of pedestrians hired camels on condition that the carrier would carry whoever among them fell ill – the contract is void. In al-Asl: If they stipulated that one would ride then another, and so on, that is permissible. In al-Khulāsah: He hired to arrive in twenty days to a place but arrived in twenty-five days – he deducts from the hire proportionally, and this is sound according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. In al-Khulāsah: A man hired camels for Hajj, then they differed on the time of departure – the word is that of the one who wants to depart at the known time. In al-Muhīt: He hired an unspecified donkey to a place – not permissible because it is a single contract and the subject matter is unknown in a way that leads to dispute. He hired a specific donkey to a place, it weakened before arrival – he must bring another because the contract does not dissolve in this case. If it was specifically identified, he need not bring another and the contract dissolves. If a man hired two donkeys for ten as a single bundle to carry twenty fayz, and he loaded ten on each, the hire is divided according to the hire of each donkey. He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (If it perishes due to an extra rider, he guarantees half) meaning if he hires a donkey and adds another rider on it, he guarantees half the value, and weight is not considered because the light rider may injure the donkey and the heavy rider may be easy due to his horsemanship, and because a human is not weighed so it cannot be known by weight, so the ruling is attached to number like injuries in the chapter of injuries. This is if the donkey can carry two; if it cannot, he guarantees the full value. This was mentioned in al-Kāfī. They said: This is if the extra rider holds himself; if it is a child who cannot hold himself, he guarantees according to his weight. In al-Nihāyah: The restriction to an extra rider is to exclude the case where he carries it on his shoulder, then he guarantees the full value because his weight and that of the carrier are concentrated in one place, which is harder for the donkey. Al-Ḥaddādī said: The extra rider is an example and not a restriction, so even if the hirer makes himself the extra rider and someone else the original, the ruling is the same. In Ghāyat al-Bayān: It is restricted to being an extra rider because if he seats a stranger in the saddle, he becomes a usurper and no hire is due. Qāḍīkhān said: He hired a donkey to ride to a place, then loaded a young child on it, and it perished – he guarantees its value as if he loaded a load. He made the guarantee of half absolute, covering whether it perishes before or after arrival. He said: He owes all the hire if it perishes after reaching his destination, and half the value if it perishes before. In al-Muhīṭ: If it perishes after reaching from riding, he owes the full hire and half the value, whether the extra rider is lighter or heavier. As for the hire, because he received the contracted benefit; as for the guarantee, because the destruction happened by their riding and it is not clear who is liable – the owner has the option to hold the extra rider or the hirer liable. If he holds the hirer liable, he cannot claim back; if he holds the extra rider liable, he can claim back if he was a hirer, otherwise not. In al-Khāniyyah: If the owner of the donkey wants to hold the extra rider liable for half the value, he has that right. In al-Tātārkhāniyyah: He hired a donkey to carry ten qafz, then he sublet it to another who loaded twenty, and it perished – the owner chooses whom to hold liable: if he holds the second liable, he can claim from the first because he deceived him; if he holds the first liable, he cannot claim from the second. I say: It should be distinguished: if he knew he was a hirer as mentioned, he should not claim from the first; if he knew he was the owner or did not know, he should claim. The author made the extra rider absolute, covering whether he is an extra rider for the whole period or part of it. In al-Muhīṭ: He hired a donkey for going and returning with its fodder, rode it going loaded goods, and added an extra rider returning – he owes the hire of its like for going because the contract was void due to ignorance of the fodder, and for returning two rode it and it died – he owes half the value and whatever was added of the load, determined by experts. This is if he did not ride on the load; if he rode on it, he guarantees the full value because it bears his weight and the load. If he hired a carrier for a child with it and it died, he guarantees according to the child. Similarly, if the camel gave birth and he loaded its young on it. It is restricted to perishing because if it survived, he owes the full hire.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling from the chapter of Ijarah in the Hanafi school, expanding the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The core ruling is: if a person hires an animal and adds an extra rider (irdaf) without the owner's permission, and the animal dies as a result, the hirer guarantees half the value of the animal. The reasoning is that the destruction is caused by two riders jointly (the hirer and the extra rider), and since both are humans whose weight cannot be precisely measured, the liability is divided by number, not weight. The commentary then provides several branches: if the animal cannot carry two, the hirer guarantees the full value; if the extra rider is a child who cannot hold himself, he guarantees according to his weight; if the extra rider is seated in the saddle (making him a usurper), the hirer is not liable for anything. The passage also discusses scenarios where the animal perishes after reaching the destination (full hire plus half value) vs. before (no full hire). It further explains that the owner has the option to hold either the hirer or the extra rider liable for the half-value, with subrogation rules. The commentary cites various sources like al-Muhit, al-Khaniyyah, and al-Tatarkhaniyyah, and the commentator adds his own preference for distinguishing cases where the extra rider's status is known.

Key Terms
الإرداف (al-irdāf): Adding an extra rider on a hired animal without the owner's permission
الرديف (al-radīf): The extra rider who is added behind the hirer on the hired animal
الجناية (al-jināyah): Injury or tort; the chapter of tort law in fiqh

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man hires a donkey that can carry two riders. He adds an adult friend as an extra rider without permission. The donkey dies. How much must the hirer guarantee?
A) The full value
B) Half the value
C) Nothing, because the extra rider was at fault
D) Half the value, but only if the extra rider was heavier

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when an extra rider is added without permission and the hired animal perishes, the hirer guarantees half the value if the animal could carry two riders, and full otherwise, based on qiyas to injury law where liability is divided by number.

Liability for Exceeding the Named Load in Ijara
Expands the ruling on exceeding the named load

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for proportional liability when a hired animal perishes due to overloading and apply it to scenarios involving joint loading and capacity.

Core Idea
When a hired animal perishes from overloading, the hirer guarantees only the proportional excess weight if the animal could bear the total load.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rāʾiq expands on the matn ruling regarding a hirer who loads more than the agreed amount on a hired animal. The core ruling is that liability is divided proportionally based on the ratio of the excess load to the total load, provided the animal could bear the combined weight. The text also addresses objections, joint loading by owner and hirer, and the difference between overloading and over-distance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic scenario and ruling
Start with the main case: a hirer loads extra weight on a hired animal and it dies. The author rules that the hirer guarantees only the excess by weight, because the death was caused by both permitted and unpermitted factors.
This is a qiyas: the total load is divided into permitted and excess parts; liability follows the cause.
2
Distinguish sub-rulings based on animal's capacity
If the animal could not bear even the named load, there was no permission for any load, so the hirer guarantees full value. If it could bear the total but the hirer added something else (not an increase on the named), full value is due for lack of permission.
The capacity condition is a key determinant.
3
Examine the grinding ox objection
Al-Akmal raises an objection: hiring an ox to grind a set amount, then increasing the quantity, incurs full liability even though the increase is of the same type. The author resolves this by noting that grinding is gradual; once the agreed amount is ground, permission ends.
This distinction shows that the rule depends on the nature of the service.
4
Analyze joint loading and order scenarios
The passage from al-Dhakhīrah and al-Khulāsah details cases where the owner participates: if owner alone loads, no hirer liability; if both load together in one sack, hirer pays 1/4; if in two sacks, no liability; if hirer loads first, full liability? Actually the text says if hirer loads first and owner later? The al-Khulāsah gives: if hirer loads first, then owner, the hirer guarantees half. This shows the interplay of permission and responsibility.
The order of loading affects liability because the owner's permission is implied when he loads after the hirer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وبالزيادة على الحمل المسمى ما زاد) يعني إذا استأجر دابة ليحمل عليها قدراً فحمل عليها أكثر منه فعطبت يضمن ما زاد بالثقل لأنها هلكت بمأذون وغيره فانقسم عليهما. هذا إذا كانت الدابة تطيق ذلك، فلو كانت لا تطيق مثله يضمن جميع القيمة لعدم الإذن فيه . هذا إذا حمل المسمى وزاد عليه وإن حمل عليها غيره فهلكت وجب عليه جميع القيمة لعدم الإذن. قال الأكمل : ونوقض بما إذا استأجر ثوراً ليطحن عليه مقداراً فزاد فهلك يضمن جميع القيمة وإن كانت الزيادة من جنسه ، وفرق بينهما بأن الطحن يكون شيئاً فشيئاً فإذا طحن القدر المسمى فقد انتهى الإذن ويطحن غيره معه فقد تعدى فيضمن جميع القيمة . قيد بكونه زاد على المعتاد لأنه إن زاد على المسافة فهلكت يضمن جميع القيمة لعدم الإذن في الزيادة. وقيد بكونه حمل عليها لأن رب الدابة لو كان هو الذي حمل عليها فلا ضمان على المستأجر . قال في الذخيرة : استأجر دابة ليحمل عليها عشرة مخاتيم من الحنطة فجعل في الجوالق عشرين من الحنطة وأمر المكاري أن يحمل هو عليها فحمل هو ولم يشاركه المستكري فهلكت لا ضمان عليه أصلاً، ولو حمل ذلك عليها رب الدابة والمستكري جميعاً ووضعاه على ظهر الدابة فهلكت الدابة ضمن المستكري ربع القيمة هذا إذا كان في جولق واحد ولو جعلها في جولقين وحمل كل واحد منهما جولقاً ووضعا على الدابة جميعاً لا يضمن المستأجر شيئاً ويجعل حمل المستأجر ما كان مستحقاً له بالعقد .اهـ. وفي الخلاصة : هذا إذا حمل المستأجر أولاً، وإن حمل رب الدابة أولاً ثم المستأجر فهلكت ضمن نصف القيمة. وفي الأصل : إذا استأجر دابة ليركبها فلبس من الثياب
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And for the excess over the named load, the excess) meaning if he hires a donkey to carry a certain amount, and he loads more than that on it and it perishes, he guarantees the excess by weight because it perished by what was permitted and what was not, so it is divided between them. This is if the donkey can bear that; if it cannot bear its like, he guarantees the full value due to lack of permission. This is if he loaded the named amount and increased. If he loaded something else on it and it perished, he owes the full value due to lack of permission. Al-Akmal said: It is objected by the case of hiring an ox to grind a quantity, and he increased and it died – he guarantees the full value even though the increase was of the same type. The difference is that grinding is done bit by bit, so when he grinds the named amount, permission ends, and grinding other with it is transgression, so he guarantees the full value. It is restricted to increasing the load because if he increases the distance and it perishes, he guarantees the full value due to lack of permission for the increase. It is restricted to him loading it because if the owner of the donkey loaded it, there is no liability on the hirer. In al-Dhakhīrah: He hired a donkey to carry ten makhātīm of wheat, and he put twenty in the sack and ordered the carrier to load it, and he loaded it without the hirer's participation – it died, no liability on him at all. If both the owner and the hirer loaded it together and placed it on the donkey's back, and the donkey died – the hirer guarantees a quarter of the value if it was in one sack; if in two sacks, each carrying one sack and placing both on the donkey, the hirer guarantees nothing, and the hirer's load is considered what he was entitled to by contract. In al-Khulāsah: This is if the hirer loaded first; if the owner loaded first then the hirer, and it died, he guarantees half the value. In al-Asl: If he hires a donkey to ride, and he puts on clothes...
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage expands the matn ruling on exceeding the named load. The basic rule: when a hirer loads more than the agreed amount on a hired animal, and the animal dies from the overload, the hirer guarantees only the proportion of the excess weight relative to the total load, because the death was caused by both the permitted load and the excess. However, if the animal could not bear even the named load (i.e., it was too weak), the hirer guarantees the full value because there was no permission for such loading. The text distinguishes this from the case of hiring an ox to grind, where increasing the quantity incurs full liability because grinding is a gradual process; once the agreed amount is done, permission ends. The passage also discusses scenarios where the owner participates in loading: if the owner loads alone, the hirer is not liable; if both load, liability is divided. The final point from al-Asl is about riding and wearing clothes, which is cut off but generally means that if the hirer wears extra clothes, it may be considered an increase.

Key Terms
الزيادة على الحمل المسمى (al-ziyādah ʿalā al-ḥaml al-musammā): Loading a hired animal with more than the amount specified in the contract
الضمان (al-ḍamān): Financial liability to compensate for damage or loss

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in the passage, if a hired animal dies because it was overloaded with 12 sacks when the agreement was for 8 sacks, and the animal could bear 12 sacks, how is liability calculated?
A) Full liability because 4 sacks excess is a significant increase.
B) Liability for 4/12 = 1/3 of the animal's value.
C) Liability for 4/8 = 1/2 of the animal's value.
D) No liability because the animal could bear the total load.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a hired animal perishes from being overloaded beyond the agreed amount, the hirer guarantees only the proportional value of the excess weight if the animal could bear the total load; otherwise, full liability applies.

Owner's Option in Double Riding of Hired Animal
Ruling on owner's option to sue either rider when hired animal dies from double riding.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a hired animal is double-ridden and dies, and identify the owner's option to sue either rider.

Core Idea
The owner may sue either rider; the second rider can recover from the first only if he was a sub-hirer.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a common scenario in ijarah: when a hired animal is used by two persons beyond the contract and dies. The Hanafi school gives the owner flexibility to claim damages from either party, with specific rules on who can seek recourse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the damage
The animal was hired for riding, but a second person rode it (double riding) and the animal died. Determine the unauthorized act and the resulting loss.
The second rider (radif) rides without a separate contract from the owner.
2
State the owner's option
The owner may choose to sue either the original hirer (musta'jir) or the second rider (radif) for the full value of the animal.
This is a khiyar (option) for the owner, not a joint liability.
3
Explain consequence if owner sues the hirer
If the owner holds the hirer liable, the hirer must pay but cannot recover anything from the second rider.
The hirer is responsible for the entire animal because he allowed the second rider.
4
Explain consequence if owner sues the second rider
If the owner holds the second rider liable, the second rider pays. He then may recover the amount from the original hirer only if the second rider was also a hirer (i.e., had his own rental contract).
If the second rider was merely a guest rider (no contract), he cannot recover.
5
Note the condition for recovery
The second rider can only recover from the hirer if he himself was a hirer (sub-hirer) and the original hirer misled him or failed to inform him of the terms.
The text from al-Khaniyya adds that the owner may claim half the value from the second rider if he chooses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإجارة باب ما يجوز من الإجارة وما يكون خلافاً فيها عليه، وأما الضمان فلأن التلف حصل بركوبهما ولم يبين من عليه الضمان فالمالك بالخيار إن شاء ضمن الرديف وإن شاء ضمن المستأجر ، فإن ضمن المستأجر لا يرجع بما ضمن، وإن ضمن الرديف يرجع إن كان مستأجراً وإلا فلا. وفي الخانية فإذا أراد صاحب الدابة أن يضمن الرديف نصف القيمة كان له ذلك. وفي التتارخانية : استأجر دابة ليحمل عليها عشرة أقفزة فأجرها من غيره فحمل عليها عشرين فتلفت يخير المالك في التضمين إن شاء ضمن الثاني ويرجع على الأول لأنه غره، وإن ضمن الأول لا يرجع على الثاني .اهـ. وأقول : ينبغي أن يفصل بأنه إن علم أنه مستأجر لما ذكر ينبغي أن لا يرجع على الأول، وإن علم أنه مالك أو لم يعلم ينبغي أن يرجع وأطلق المؤلف في الإرداف فشمل ما إذا أردف في كل المدة أو بعضها. وفي المحيط : استأجر دابة ذاهباً وراجعاً بعلفها فركبها ذاهباً وحمل عليها متاعاً وأردف آخر راجعاً فعليه أجرة مثلها في الذهاب لأن الأجارة وقعت فاسدة لجهالة العلف، وفي الرجوع ركبها اثنان فهلكت فعليه نصف القيمة ولما زاد من الحمل ويعرف ذلك بالرجوع إلى أهل الخبرة. وهذا إذا لم يركب على الحمل، إما إذا ركب عليه يضمن جميع قيمتها لأنه يحتمل ثقله وثقل الحمل عليها. ولو استأجر محمل الولد معها فتلفت ضمن بقدر الولد وكذا لو ولدت الناقة فحمل ولدها عليها. وقيد بالعطب لأنها لو سلمت يجب عليه الأجر تماماً .
Book of Ijarah, Chapter on what is permissible in Ijarah and what is contrary to it. ... As for liability, because destruction occurred by both riding and it was not clarified who is liable, the owner has the option: if he wishes he may hold the second rider liable, and if he wishes he may hold the hirer liable. If he holds the hirer liable, he does not recover what he paid. If he holds the second rider liable, he recovers if the second rider was a hirer, otherwise not. In al-Khaniyya: If the owner of the animal wishes to hold the second rider liable for half the value, he may do so. In al-Tatarkhaniyya: He hired an animal to carry ten qafiz, then sub-hired it to another who loaded twenty on it and it was destroyed; the owner has the option: if he wishes he may hold the second liable, and the second recovers from the first because he deceived him; if he holds the first liable, he does not recover from the second. I say: It should be detailed: if he knew he was a hirer for what was mentioned, he should not recover from the first; if he knew he was the owner or did not know, he should recover. The author's expression in 'al-irdaf' includes whether the second rider rode for the whole period or part of it. In al-Muhit: He hired an animal for going and returning with its fodder; he rode it going and loaded goods on it and carried another rider behind returning; he owes its like hire for going because the lease was invalid due to ignorance of the fodder; and for returning, two rode it and it was destroyed; he owes half the value plus the extra load, and that is known by consulting experts. This is if he did not ride on the load; if he rode on it, he is liable for the entire value because it bears his weight and the weight of the load. If he hired a vehicle for a child with her and it was destroyed, he is liable proportional to the child; similarly if a she-camel gives birth and he loads its young on her. The restriction to destruction is because if it survived, the hire is due in full.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings on liability when a hired animal is used beyond the contract, specifically double riding and overloading. The opening statement gives the general rule: if a hired animal is ridden by two persons and dies, the owner may sue either the primary hirer or the second rider. If he sues the hirer, the hirer cannot recover from the second rider. If he sues the second rider, the second rider may recover from the hirer only if the second rider was also a sub-hirer; if he was merely a rider without a contract, he cannot recover. The text then cites various authoritative sources. In al-Khaniyya, the owner may specifically claim half the value from the second rider. In al-Tatarkhaniyya, a case of overloading is given: if a person hires an animal to carry 10 qafiz, sub-hires it, and the sub-hirer loads 20 qafiz causing destruction, the owner can sue either; the second can recover from the first due to deception. The commentator adds a refinement based on knowledge. Al-Muhit presents a complex case of a round trip with invalid lease due to unknown fodder, and the liability for the return journey when two ride. The passage concludes with cases of extra weight from a child or newborn, and that if the animal survives, full hire is due. All examples reinforce the Hanafi principle that liability is apportioned based on what is authorized and what is extra.

Key Terms
الرديف (al-irdaf): The person who rides behind the rider on the same animal.
الضمان (al-daman): Liability for compensation due to damage or destruction of the hired animal.
المستأجر (al-musta'jir): The person who hires the animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, if a hired animal dies from double riding and the owner sues the hirer, can the hirer recover from the second rider?
A) Yes, always
B) Yes, if the second rider was a sub-hirer
C) No, never
D) Only if the owner agrees

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the owner of a hired animal that dies due to double riding has the option to sue either the hirer or the second rider, with specific recourse rules for the second rider.

Liability for Overloading and Sub-Hiring
Ruling on sub-hiring and overloading causing destruction, with chain of recourse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on sub-hiring and overloading of a hired animal, and identify the owner's option to sue either party with the chain of recourse.

Core Idea
The sub-hirer who overloads is liable; he can recover from the original hirer if deceived.

The passage continues with a scenario from al-Tatarkhaniyya where a hirer sub-hires an animal to carry a specific weight, but the sub-hirer exceeds it, causing destruction. This lesson explores the owner's options and the chain of recourse based on deception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A hires an animal to carry 10 qafiz, sub-hires to B, but B loads 20 qafiz and the animal dies.
2
State the owner's option
The owner may sue either A (original hirer) or B (sub-hirer) for the full value.
3
Explain recourse if owner sues B
If owner sues B, B can recover from A because A deceived B by not specifying the weight limit or by giving a false impression that the animal could carry more.
Deception (taghrir) is the key element.
4
Explain recourse if owner sues A
If owner sues A, A cannot recover from B because A is the primary responsible party.
5
Note the commentator's refinement
The commentator (Ibn Nujaym) adds: if B knew that A was a hirer (not owner) and still overloaded, then B cannot recover from A; but if B thought A was the owner or didn't know, B can recover.
Knowledge of the status affects the right to recourse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإجارة باب ما يجوز من الإجارة وما يكون خلافاً فيها عليه، وأما الضمان فلأن التلف حصل بركوبهما ولم يبين من عليه الضمان فالمالك بالخيار إن شاء ضمن الرديف وإن شاء ضمن المستأجر ، فإن ضمن المستأجر لا يرجع بما ضمن، وإن ضمن الرديف يرجع إن كان مستأجراً وإلا فلا. وفي الخانية فإذا أراد صاحب الدابة أن يضمن الرديف نصف القيمة كان له ذلك. وفي التتارخانية : استأجر دابة ليحمل عليها عشرة أقفزة فأجرها من غيره فحمل عليها عشرين فتلفت يخير المالك في التضمين إن شاء ضمن الثاني ويرجع على الأول لأنه غره، وإن ضمن الأول لا يرجع على الثاني .اهـ. وأقول : ينبغي أن يفصل بأنه إن علم أنه مستأجر لما ذكر ينبغي أن لا يرجع على الأول، وإن علم أنه مالك أو لم يعلم ينبغي أن يرجع وأطلق المؤلف في الإرداف فشمل ما إذا أردف في كل المدة أو بعضها. وفي المحيط : استأجر دابة ذاهباً وراجعاً بعلفها فركبها ذاهباً وحمل عليها متاعاً وأردف آخر راجعاً فعليه أجرة مثلها في الذهاب لأن الأجارة وقعت فاسدة لجهالة العلف، وفي الرجوع ركبها اثنان فهلكت فعليه نصف القيمة ولما زاد من الحمل ويعرف ذلك بالرجوع إلى أهل الخبرة. وهذا إذا لم يركب على الحمل، إما إذا ركب عليه يضمن جميع قيمتها لأنه يحتمل ثقله وثقل الحمل عليها. ولو استأجر محمل الولد معها فتلفت ضمن بقدر الولد وكذا لو ولدت الناقة فحمل ولدها عليها. وقيد بالعطب لأنها لو سلمت يجب عليه الأجر تماماً .
Book of Ijarah, Chapter on what is permissible in Ijarah and what is contrary to it. ... As for liability, because destruction occurred by both riding and it was not clarified who is liable, the owner has the option: if he wishes he may hold the second rider liable, and if he wishes he may hold the hirer liable. If he holds the hirer liable, he does not recover what he paid. If he holds the second rider liable, he recovers if the second rider was a hirer, otherwise not. In al-Khaniyya: If the owner of the animal wishes to hold the second rider liable for half the value, he may do so. In al-Tatarkhaniyya: He hired an animal to carry ten qafiz, then sub-hired it to another who loaded twenty on it and it was destroyed; the owner has the option: if he wishes he may hold the second liable, and the second recovers from the first because he deceived him; if he holds the first liable, he does not recover from the second. I say: It should be detailed: if he knew he was a hirer for what was mentioned, he should not recover from the first; if he knew he was the owner or did not know, he should recover. The author's expression in 'al-irdaf' includes whether the second rider rode for the whole period or part of it. In al-Muhit: He hired an animal for going and returning with its fodder; he rode it going and loaded goods on it and carried another rider behind returning; he owes its like hire for going because the lease was invalid due to ignorance of the fodder; and for returning, two rode it and it was destroyed; he owes half the value plus the extra load, and that is known by consulting experts. This is if he did not ride on the load; if he rode on it, he is liable for the entire value because it bears his weight and the weight of the load. If he hired a vehicle for a child with her and it was destroyed, he is liable proportional to the child; similarly if a she-camel gives birth and he loads its young on her. The restriction to destruction is because if it survived, the hire is due in full.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings on liability when a hired animal is used beyond the contract, specifically double riding and overloading. The opening statement gives the general rule: if a hired animal is ridden by two persons and dies, the owner may sue either the primary hirer or the second rider. If he sues the hirer, the hirer cannot recover from the second rider. If he sues the second rider, the second rider may recover from the hirer only if the second rider was also a sub-hirer; if he was merely a rider without a contract, he cannot recover. The text then cites various authoritative sources. In al-Khaniyya, the owner may specifically claim half the value from the second rider. In al-Tatarkhaniyya, a case of overloading is given: if a person hires an animal to carry 10 qafiz, sub-hires it, and the sub-hirer loads 20 qafiz causing destruction, the owner can sue either; the second can recover from the first due to deception. The commentator adds a refinement based on knowledge. Al-Muhit presents a complex case of a round trip with invalid lease due to unknown fodder, and the liability for the return journey when two ride. The passage concludes with cases of extra weight from a child or newborn, and that if the animal survives, full hire is due. All examples reinforce the Hanafi principle that liability is apportioned based on what is authorized and what is extra.

Key Terms
الغار (al-gharr): Deception or misrepresentation that causes loss.
التضمين (al-tadmin): Holding liable for compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the sub-hiring case, if the owner sues the sub-hirer (B), under what condition can B recover from the original hirer (A)?
A) B can always recover
B) B can recover only if A was the owner
C) B can recover if A deceived him about the load capacity
D) B can never recover

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a hired animal is overloaded due to sub-hiring, the owner may sue either party; the sub-hirer may recover from the original if deceived, with a refinement based on the sub-hirer's knowledge.

Overloading Beyond Specified Weight in Ijarah
Ruling on overloading hired animals with liability apportionment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability for overloading a hired animal and apply it to scenarios involving capacity and authorization.

Core Idea
Liability for overloading is proportional if the animal can bear extra weight; full value if it cannot or if the act is unauthorized.

This lesson examines a classic ijarah ruling: what happens when a hirer loads more than the agreed weight? The Hanafi school distinguishes based on the animal's capacity and whether the extra load was authorized. We'll explore the general rule and its application through several nuanced cases from the Hanafi texts.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
From the matn: if the animal can bear the extra weight, liability is proportional to the extra weight; if it cannot, full value is owed.
This is the default rule.
2
Analyze the condition of capacity
The animal's capability (tutiq) is key. Determine whether the extra load is within normal limits.
Applies to both carrying and riding.
3
Examine the grinding exception
Grinding is incremental; once the agreed amount is ground, permission ends. Extra grinding is a separate transgression, leading to full liability regardless of capacity.
Al-Akmal's distinction.
4
Apply to multi-party loading
If the owner helps load, liability is apportioned based on contribution. Cases from al-Dhakhira show scenarios with one or two sacks.
The hirer's share is based on what he loaded.
5
Consider other variables
Clothing, saddles, distance, rider weight – all affect liability if they deviate from normal.
Only the extra proportion is liable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وبالزيادة على الحمل المسمى ما زاد يعني إذا استأجر دابة ليحمل عليها قدراً فحمل عليها أكثر منه فعطبت يضمن ما زاد بالثقل لأنها هلكت بمأذون وغيره فانقسم عليهما. هذا إذا كانت الدابة تطيق ذلك، فلو كانت لا تطيق مثله يضمن جميع القيمة لعدم الإذن فيه . هذا إذا حمل المسمى وزاد عليه وإن حمل عليها غيره فهلكت وجب عليه جميع القيمة لعدم الإذن. قال الأكمل : ونوقض بما إذا استأجر ثوراً ليطحن عليه مقداراً فزاد فهلك يضمن جميع القيمة وإن كانت الزيادة من جنسه ، وفرق بينهما بأن الطحن يكون شيئاً فشيئاً فإذا طحن القدر المسمى فقد انتهى الإذن ويطحن غيره معه فقد تعدى فيضمن جميع القيمة . قيد بكونه زاد على المعتاد لأنه إن زاد على المسافة فهلكت يضمن جميع القيمة لعدم الإذن في الزيادة. وقيد بكونه حمل عليها لأن رب الدابة لو كان هو الذي حمل عليها فلا ضمان على المستأجر . قال في الذخيرة : استأجر دابة ليحمل عليها عشرة مخاتيم من الحنطة فجعل في الجوالق عشرين من الحنطة وأمر المكاري أن يحمل هو عليها فحمل هو ولم يشاركه المستكري فهلكت لا ضمان عليه أصلاً، ولو حمل ذلك عليها رب الدابة والمستكري جميعاً ووضعاه على ظهر الدابة فهلكت الدابة ضمن المستكري ربع القيمة هذا إذا كان في جولق واحد ولو جعلها في جولقين وحمل كل واحد منهما جولقاً ووضعا على الدابة جميعاً لا يضمن المستأجر شيئاً ويجعل حمل المستأجر ما كان مستحقاً له بالعقد .اهـ. وفي الخلاصة : هذا إذا حمل المستأجر أولاً، وإن حمل رب الدابة أولاً ثم المستأجر فهلكت ضمن نصف القيمة. وفي الأصل : إذا استأجر دابة ليركبها فلبس من الثياب وبالضرب والكبح ونزع السرج والإكاف أو الأسراج بما لا بمثله وسلوك طريق يسرج أكثر مما كان يلبس وركب الدابة فهلكت ؛ إن لبس ما يلبس الناس فلا ضمان عليه، وإن لبس ما لا يلبسه الناس ضمن ما زاد بحسابه. وفي الخانية : استأجر دابة ليركبها إنساناً فأركبها امرأة بآلة أو رجلاً بسرج فهلكت لا ضمان عليه ولا على الراكب إلا أن يعلم أن مثل الدابة لا تطيق ذلك فيضمن جميع القيمة. وفي الأصل : استأجر حماراً بسرج فأسرجه بسرج لا يسرج به مثله فهو : ضامن مقدار ما زاد باتفاق الروايات وإن كان أخف من الأول أو مثله فلا ضمان عليه . هذا إذا كانت الدابة توكف بمثله وإن كانت لا توكف بمثله يضمن جميع القيمة. وفي قاضيخان : وإن تلفت فله الأجرة تماماً، ولو علم أنها تطيق قبل فله تمام الأجرة، وإذا هلكت يضمن ولا تجب الأجرة. هذا إذا جعل الأقل والزيادة في جولق واحد، ولو جعل الزيادة في جولق منفردة وحملها ضمن القيمة. وفي المحيط : استأجر دابة ليحمل عليها امرأة فولدت فحمل ولدها معها عليها يضمن بقدر الولد .
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And by the increase over the specified load, what is increased.) Meaning: if he hires an animal to carry a certain amount and loads more than that and it is destroyed, he is liable for the increase proportional to the weight because it was destroyed by both authorized and unauthorized, so it is apportioned between them. This is if the animal can bear that; if it cannot bear the like, he is liable for the entire value due to lack of permission. This is if he loaded the specified amount and added to it; if he loaded something else on it and it was destroyed, he owes the entire value due to lack of permission. Al-Akmal said: It is objected with the case of hiring an ox to grind a certain amount and he increased and it died; he is liable for the entire value even though the increase was of the same type. The difference between them is that grinding is piece by piece; when he grinds the specified amount, permission ends, and grinding other with it is transgression, so he is liable for the entire value. It is restricted to where he increased beyond the customary because if he increased the distance and it died, he is liable for the entire value due to lack of permission for the increase. It is restricted to his loading because if the owner of the animal loaded it, there is no liability on the hirer. In al-Dhakhira: He hired an animal to carry ten makhateem of wheat; he put twenty of wheat in the sack and ordered the muleteer to load it; he loaded it without the hirer's participation and it died; there is no liability on him at all. If the owner and the hirer both loaded it and placed it on the back of the animal and it died, the hirer is liable for a quarter of the value; this is if in one sack. If he put it in two sacks and each carried one sack and both placed on the animal, the hirer is not liable for anything, and the hirer's load is considered what he is entitled to by contract. In al-Khulasa: This is if the hirer loaded first; if the owner loaded first then the hirer and it died, he is liable for half the value. In al-Asl: If he hires an animal to ride and wears clothing and by striking and pulling and removing the saddle and pack-saddle or saddles with what is not its like and taking a road that... more than he used to wear and rides and it dies: if he wears what people wear, no liability; if he wears what people do not wear, he is liable for the increase proportionally. In al-Khaniyya: He hires an animal for a man to ride; he lets a woman ride it with its gear or a man with a saddle and it dies; no liability on him or the rider unless he knows that such an animal cannot bear that, then he is liable for the entire value. In al-Asl: He hires a donkey with a saddle and puts on it a saddle that is not like it; he is liable for the amount of increase by consensus of narrations; if it is lighter or equal, no liability. This is if the animal can bear the like; if it cannot bear the like, he is liable for the entire value. In Qadikhan: If it is destroyed, he owes the full hire; if he knew it could bear before, he owes the full hire; if it dies, he is liable and the hire is not due. This is if the lesser and increase are in one sack; if he puts the increase in a separate sack and loads it, he is liable for the value. In al-Muhit: He hires an animal to carry a woman; she gives birth and he loads the child with her; he is liable proportional to the child.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage begins with the matn 'Wa bil-ziyadati 'ala al-haml al-musamma ma zad' and the commentary explains the ruling on overloading a hired animal. The general rule: if the animal can bear the extra weight, the hirer is liable only for the proportion of the extra weight that caused the damage; if the animal cannot bear it, he is liable for the full value. The text makes a crucial distinction between loading the same type of goods (like wheat) versus a different type or additional service (like grinding vs carrying). The commentary draws from al-Akmal, noting an objection about grinding an ox: griding is incremental and permission ends when the specified amount is ground, so any extra is transgression leading to full liability. The passage then provides several detailed cases from al-Dhakhira, al-Khulasa, al-Asl, al-Khaniyya, and al-Muhit, covering scenarios where the owner assists in loading, where the hirer wears unusual clothing, where a different rider is placed, and where a different saddle is used. The underlying principle is that the hirer's liability depends on whether the act was authorized or not; if the animal dies from an unauthorized act, full liability; if from a mix, proportional liability. The case of a woman giving birth highlights that the extra load (the child) is treated as unauthorized increase, leading to proportional liability.

Key Terms
الزيادة على الحمل المسمى (al-ziyada 'ala al-haml al-musamma): Increasing the load beyond what was specified in the ijarah contract.
الجوالق (al-jawaliq): A large sack used for carrying grain or goods on animals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a hired animal is loaded with more than the agreed weight and dies, when is the hirer liable for only the proportional increase?
A) When the animal can bear the extra weight
B) When the owner helped load
C) When the extra load is of a different type
D) When the hirer wore unusual clothing

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school apportions liability for overloading a hired animal based on its capacity and the nature of the extra load, with full liability only when the animal cannot bear the extra weight or the act is entirely unauthorized.

Liability for Striking a Hired Animal
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability for striking hired animal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on liability for striking a hired animal, explain the Qiyas used, and identify when liability is imposed.

Core Idea
Imam holds hirer liable for any striking; Sahibayn exempt if customary.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the liability of a hirer who strikes or pulls the reins of a hired animal, causing its death. The disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hinges on whether customary actions are included in the contract's authorization. The discussion extends to analogous cases like striking a hired slave, a father disciplining his child, and a teacher with permission. By the end, you will be able to articulate each position and its practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the ruling
Extract the core legal question: Is a hirer liable for striking or pulling (kabh) a hired animal if the act is customary? Note that the matn states liability, but the commentary reveals a dispute.
Focus on the word 'يضمن' (liable) and the conditional 'إذا هلكت' (if it dies).
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Imam holds the hirer liable because customary actions are conditioned upon safety; striking is unnecessary for driving and only for intensification, so it exceeds authorization.
Imam uses a rational argument: driving can be done without striking.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
The Sahibayn hold no liability for customary acts because the absolute contract includes what is customary; striking is normal for driving.
They argue that the animal does not understand commands, unlike a slave, so striking is necessary.
4
Analyze the Qiyas with a hired slave
The text compares striking a hired animal to striking a hired slave: consensus says the hirer is liable for striking the slave because the slave understands and striking is unnecessary. The Sahibayn distinguish by saying the animal lacks understanding.
Consider the illa (effective cause): the slave's understanding vs. the animal's lack thereof.
5
Apply to derivative cases
The dispute extends to a father or guardian striking a minor for discipline, and to teachers with permission. Identify how the principles apply and where consensus exists (e.g., with owner's permission or excessive harshness).
Note the exceptions: permission from owner eliminates liability; harshness always imposes liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله: (وبالضرب والكبح) أي يضمن إذا هلكت منهما. وفي المغرب الكبح ضرب الدابة باللجام وهو أن يجذبها إلى نفسه. وهذا عند الإمام. وقالا : لا يضمن إذا فعل فعلاً معتاداً لأن المطلق يدخل تحت المتعارف فكان هالكاً بالمأذون به وللإمام أن المتعارف مقيد بشرط السلامة لأن السوق يتحقق بدونه وإنما تضرب للمبالغة، وهذا بخلاف ما إذا ضرب العبد المستأجر للخدمة حيث يضمن بالإجماع . والفرق لهما أنه يأمر وينهي لفهمه فلا ضرورة إلى ضربه وظاهر ما في الهداية أن للمستأجر. الضرب ولا إثم عليه. وفي غاية البيان: إن ضرب الدابة يكون متعدياً للضمان وفيها موجباً أن الإمام رجع إلى قولهما . وأما ضرب دابة نفسه فقال في القنية : لا يضربها أصلاً وإن كانت ملكه ثم قال : لا يخاصم ضارب الحيوان فيما يحتاج إليه للتأديب ويخاصم فيما زاد عليه، وعلى هذا الخلاف المذكور ضرب الأب أو الوصي للصغير إذا لم يجاوز ضرب مثله للتأديب حيث تجب الدية والكفارة عنده وعندهما لا تجب الدية لأن الضرب لإصلاح الصغير متعارف وفيه منفعة له فكان كضرب المعلم بل أولى بخلاف ضرب الزوج لأن لمنفعة نفسه فيشترط فيه السلام وللإمام أن منفعة الصغير كالواقع له لقيام البعضية بينهما ألا ترى أن الشهادة له جعلت كشهادته لنفسه، وبخلاف ضرب المعلم بإذن الأب لأن الإذن من الأب : من الولاية، وإذا صح كأن الأب معيناً ولا ضمان على المعين. وليس له أن يضرب أخيه الصغير على ترك الصلاة وأطلق في الضرب والكبح وهو محمول على ما إذا كان بغير إذن صاحبها ففي التتارخانية استأجرها ليركبها فضربها فماتت. فإن كان بإذن صاحبها وأصاب الموضع لا يضمن بالإجماع. وفي العتابية فإن عنف في السير ضمن إجماعاً، والمعلم والمؤدب واستاذ الحرفة يضمن بالضرب فإن كان بإذن لم يضمن اهـ. وفي جامع الفصولين : استأجر حماراً لحمل متاع ولم يكن صاحب المتاع. معه فمرض الحمار في صحيح لما له
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And by striking and pulling) i.e., he is liable if the animal dies from them. In al-Mughrib: 'al-kabh' means striking the animal with the bit, i.e., pulling it towards oneself. This is the view of Imam (Abu Hanifa). The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He is not liable if he does a customary act because the absolute falls under the customary, so it is destroyed by what is authorized. According to Imam, the customary is conditioned upon safety because driving is achieved without it; it is only struck for intensification. This is unlike striking a hired slave for service, where he is liable by consensus. The difference for them is that the slave understands commands and prohibitions, so there is no need to strike him. The apparent meaning in al-Hidayah is that the hirer may strike and there is no sin on him. In Ghayat al-Bayan: Striking the animal is considered transgression for liability, and it implies that Imam retracted to their view. As for striking one's own animal, in al-Qunya: He should not strike it at all even if it is his property; then he said: He does not sue the striker of an animal for what is needed for discipline, but he sues for what exceeds that. Based on this difference, striking of a father or guardian of a minor if he does not exceed the customary striking for discipline: according to him (Imam) diya and kaffara are obligatory; according to them, diya is not obligatory because striking for reform of a minor is customary and has benefit for him, so it is like striking a teacher, even more so. This is unlike striking a husband because it is for his own benefit, so safety is required. According to Imam, the benefit to the minor is like benefit to himself due to the relationship of partial identity; do you not see that his testimony for the minor is made like his testimony for himself? And unlike striking a teacher with the father's permission, because permission from the father is from guardianship, and if it is valid, it is as if the father appointed him, and there is no liability on the appointed one. He does not have the right to strike his minor brother for abandoning prayer. The ruling on striking and pulling is general and is interpreted as when done without the owner's permission. In al-Tatarkhaniyya: He hired an animal to ride it, struck it, and it died. If it was with the owner's permission and he struck the right spot, no liability by consensus. In al-Atabiyya: If he is harsh in driving, he is liable by consensus. The teacher, discipliner, and master of a craft are liable for striking; if with permission, no liability. In Jami' al-Fusulayn: He hired a donkey to carry goods and the owner of the goods was not with him; the donkey fell sick in...
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage addresses the liability for striking (darb) and pulling (kabh) a hired animal. It begins with the matn that the hirer is liable if the animal dies from these actions. The commentary explains the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Imam Abu Hanifa holds the hirer liable for any striking or pulling, even if customary, because he argues that customary actions are conditioned upon safety; striking is not necessary for driving and is only for intensification, so it is beyond what is authorized. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that if the act is customary, there is no liability because the absolute permission in the contract includes what is customary. They draw a parallel to striking a hired slave: if the slave is struck, the hirer is liable by consensus because the slave understands commands and striking is unnecessary. The text then discusses striking one's own animal: it is generally not allowed, but for discipline, no suit for customary striking. The discussion extends to striking a child for discipline: Imam holds diya and kaffara obligatory if death occurs, while Sahibayn do not, because it is customary and beneficial. The father's striking is analogized to a teacher's striking with permission. The passage also cites conditions: if the owner permits and the right spot is struck, no liability by consensus; if the hirer is harsh in driving, liability is by consensus. Teachers and craftsmen are liable for striking unless permitted. The passage ends abruptly with a case from Jami' al-Fusulayn about a donkey falling sick. The overall principle is that striking must be within customary limits and with permission; otherwise, liability attaches.

Key Terms
الكبح (al-kabh): Pulling the animal towards oneself by the bit (rein).
الضرب (al-darb): Striking the animal, e.g., with a stick or whip.
المتعارف (al-muta'arif): What is customary or conventionally accepted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because the animal is property and can be treated as the owner wishes.
B) Because the absolute contract includes customary actions, so the animal dies by an authorized act.
C) Because striking is always forbidden and invalidates the contract.
D) Because the hirer has the right to discipline the animal.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, liability for striking a hired animal depends on whether the act is customary, with the mufta bihi position imposing liability if striking is without permission or excessive.

Liability for Striking and Pulling Bridle of Rented Animal
Commentary on the liability for striking and pulling bridle of a rented animal, with an internal Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding liability for striking and pulling the bridle of a rented animal, and identify the relied-upon position.

Core Idea
Customary striking of a rented animal does not incur liability for its death, according to the relied-upon Hanafi view.

The renter of an animal may need to urge it on by striking or pulling the bridle. What happens if the animal dies from these actions? This lesson examines a classical Hanafi disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, over whether the renter is liable. We will trace the reasoning on both sides and see why the view of the Sahibayn ultimately became the operative ruling for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed actions and their legal implication
The actions are striking (darb) and pulling the bridle (kabh). The ruling in dispute is whether the renter guarantees (daman) the value of the animal if it perishes from these actions.
The opposite party in the dispute is the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani).
2
State the position of Imam Abu Hanifa
Imam holds that the renter is liable even if the action is customary, because the permission to ride is conditioned on safety.
Imam's dalil: striking is for urgency and not inherent to riding; the customary practice is restricted by the condition of safety.
3
State the position of the Sahibayn
They hold that no liability if the action is customary, because absolute permission includes customary acts.
Sahibayn's dalil: the owner's permission to ride implies permission for customary driving actions.
4
Understand the distinguishing case of striking a hired slave
Striking a hired slave results in liability by consensus, because the slave can be commanded verbally, so there is no need to strike.
This contrast highlights the principle that the need for striking differs between humans and animals.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
Imam eventually retracted and agreed with the Sahibayn, as reported in Ghayat al-Bayan. Therefore the relied-upon view is no liability for customary acts.
This is an example of a founder's opinion being revised based on stronger evidence within the school.

الكبح ضرب الدابة باللجام وهو أن يجذبها إلى نفسه. وهذا عند الإمام. وقالا : لا يضمن إذا فعل فعلاً معتاداً لأن المطلق يدخل تحت المتعارف فكان هالكاً بالمأذون به وللإمام أن المتعارف مقيد بشرط السلامة لأن السوق يتحقق بدونه وإنما تضرب للمبالغة، وهذا بخلاف ما إذا ضرب العبد المستأجر للخدمة حيث يضمن بالإجماع . والفرق لهما أنه يأمر وينهي لفهمه فلا ضرورة إلى ضربه وظاهر ما في الهداية أن للمستأجر. الضرب ولا إثم عليه. وفي غاية البيان: إن ضرب الدابة يكون متعدياً للضمان وفيها موجباً أن الإمام رجع إلى قولهما . وأما ضرب دابة نفسه فقال في القنية : لا يضربها أصلاً وإن كانت ملكه ثم قال : لا يخاصم ضارب الحيوان فيما يحتاج إليه للتأديب ويخاصم فيما زاد عليه، وعلى هذا الخلاف المذكور ضرب الأب أو الوصي للصغير إذا لم يجاوز ضرب مثله للتأديب حيث تجب الدية والكفارة عنده وعندهما لا تجب الدية لأن الضرب لإصلاح الصغير متعارف وفيه منفعة له فكان كضرب المعلم بل أولى بخلاف ضرب الزوج لأن لمنفعة نفسه فيشترط فيه السلام وللإمام أن منفعة الصغير كالواقع له لقيام البعضية بينهما ألا ترى أن الشهادة له جعلت كشهادته لنفسه، وبخلاف الطريق فترك الحمار صاحبه وترك المتاع لم يضمن للضرورة والعذر.
Book of Ijarah, chapter on what is permissible in Ijarah and what is disputed therein. And (liability results from) striking, pulling the bridle, removing the saddle or packsaddle, or putting on a saddle that is not like it, and taking a road that requires more saddle than what was worn, and riding the animal and it perished. If he wore what people wear, there is no liability; if he wore what people do not wear, he guarantees the excess proportionally. In al-Khaniyyah: He hired a beast to ride a person, and he made a woman ride with a saddling or a man with a saddle, and it perished - no liability on him nor on the rider unless he knew that such a beast cannot bear that, then he guarantees the entire value. In al-Asl: He hired a donkey with a saddle and put on it a saddle that is not used for such a donkey, so he is liable for the amount of increase by agreement of the narrations; if the saddle was lighter than the first or equal, no liability. This if the beast can bear that kind; if it cannot bear that kind, he guarantees the entire value. In Qadikhan: If it perishes, he is entitled to full rent; if he knew it could bear before, he gets full rent; if it perishes, he guarantees and rent is not obligatory. This if the lesser and the increase are in one load; if he put the increase in a separate load and carried it, he guarantees the value. This is contrary to striking a hired slave for service, where he guarantees by consensus. The distinction for them is that he (the slave) can be commanded and forbidden due to his understanding, so there is no need to strike him. The apparent meaning in al-Hidayah is that the lessee may strike and there is no sin upon him. In Ghayat al-Bayan: Striking the beast is considered transgressing for liability, and it indicates that Imam returned to their view. As for striking one's own beast, al-Qunyah says: He should not strike it at all even if it is his property; then he said: He who strikes an animal is not blamed for what is needed for discipline, and he is blamed for what exceeds that. Based on this mentioned dispute, striking of a father or guardian for a child if he does not exceed suitable discipline - according to Imam, blood money and expiation are obligatory; according to them, no penalty because striking for the child's improvement is customary and beneficial, so it is like striking of a teacher, rather more so. Contrary to striking of a husband, because it is for his own benefit, so safety is required. According to Imam, the child's benefit is like his own benefit due to the partial connection between them; do you not see that the child's testimony is treated like his own testimony? And contrary to striking of a teacher with the father's permission, because permission from the father is from guardianship, and when valid, the father becomes an assistant, and no liability on the assistant. He may not strike his minor brother for abandoning prayer. The statement about striking and pulling bridle is unrestricted and is interpreted as when done without the owner's permission. In al-TatarKhaniyyah: He hired a beast to ride it and struck it and it died; if with the owner's permission and he hit the right spot, he does not guarantee by consensus. In al-Atabiyyah: If he is harsh in driving, he guarantees by consensus. The teacher, educator, and craft master guarantee for striking; if with permission, they do not guarantee. In Jami' al-Fusulayn: He hired a donkey to carry goods, and the owner of the goods was not with him; then the donkey fell ill on the way...: not what he specified and they differed; he carried it in the sea, all of it, and if it arrives, he gets the rent; and he planted fresh grass, and he permitted for the land... the road, so he left the donkey and left the goods, he does not guarantee due to necessity and excuse.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq provides a detailed commentary on the liability (daman) that arises when a renter of an animal causes its death by striking (darb) or pulling the bridle (kabh). The matn states that the renter is liable for these actions. The commentator (Ibn Nujaym) explains that 'kabh' means pulling the donkey by the bridle toward oneself. This ruling is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The two companions (Sahibayn), Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, hold that the renter is not liable if he does a customary act, because the absolute permission for riding includes customary actions. They argue that since the owner permits riding, he implicitly permits the usual striking for driving. Imam Abu Hanifa, however, maintains that the customary practice is qualified by the condition of safety, because riding can be accomplished without striking; striking is only for urging, which is excessive. The commentator then notes that according to Ghayat al-Bayan, Imam eventually retracted his view and agreed with the Sahibayn. The passage also analogizes to other cases: striking a hired slave (where liability is unanimous), striking one's own beast (permitted for discipline but not otherwise), and striking a child by parent or guardian (Imam says liable; Sahibayn say not liable if customary). The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the Sahibayn: no guarantee if the action is customary.

Key Terms
الكبح (al-kabh): Striking the beast with the bridle, pulling it towards oneself.
الضرب (al-darb): Striking the animal, typically to urge it on.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He must guarantee the full value.
B) He must guarantee the value of the excess.
C) He is not liable.
D) He must pay blood money.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position holds that a renter is not liable for the death of a rented animal if his actions were customary, as Imam Abu Hanifa eventually agreed with the Sahibayn.

Changing Saddle or Packsaddle on a Rented Animal: Liability Dispute between Imam and Sahibayn
Commentary on liability for removing and replacing saddle or packsaddle

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability for replacing a saddle or packsaddle on a rented donkey and distinguish between the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Saddle type matters: unsuitable saddle triggers full liability; packsaddle triggers liability unless the animal is accustomed to it.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq examines a nuanced case in rental contracts (ijara): what happens when a renter removes the original saddle from a hired donkey and replaces it with a different one? The ruling hinges on the type of saddle (riding vs. packsaddle) and its suitability for the animal. Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) differed on the packsaddle, leading to distinct legal consequences. Understanding this dispute sharpens your appreciation of how the Hanafi school reasons by distinguishing between types ('jins') and relying on custom ('urf').

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and potential liability
The act is the renter removing the original saddle/packsaddle from a hired donkey and putting on a different one. Determine whether this is a transgression (ta'addi) that creates liability (daman) if the animal perishes.
Key terms: ta'addi (transgression), daman (civil liability).
2
State the position of Imam Abu Hanifa
For a riding saddle (sarj): liability only if the new saddle is unsuitable (i.e., not the kind customarily used for such donkeys). For a packsaddle (ikaf): liability even if suitable, unless the donkey can bear that type of packsaddle – otherwise, full liability.
Imam distinguishes because packsaddle is for carrying, saddle for riding; they affect the animal differently.
3
State the position of the Sahibayn
They equate the packsaddle with the saddle: liability arises only if the new saddle/packsaddle is unsuitable. No distinction between types.
The Sahibayn see packsaddle as analogous in purpose, so same rule applies.
4
Analyze the evidence (talil) for each view
Imam: Packsaddle and saddle are different genera (jins), like wheat and barley – they spread differently on the back. The permission ('idhn) covers what is similar, not what is generically different. Sahibayn: Since both are saddles, they are similar; custom ('urf) determines suitability, not generic type.
Al-Nihayah records two narrations from Imam: one full liability, one partial (excess value). The latter is more correct.
5
Identify the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The relied-upon view is that of Imam Abu Hanifa: for packsaddle, liability is for the excess value (if the animal dies due to the change). If the new saddle is unsuitable, full liability. The practical application considers custom ('urf) – e.g., whether the animal is commonly ridden bare or with a packsaddle.
Qadikhan and the later fatwa works refine the custom factor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( ونزع السرج والإكاف أو الأسراج بما لا يسرج بمثله) يعني لو استأجر حماراً مسرجاً فنزعه وأسرجه بسرج لا يسرج بمثله الحمير أو أوكفه بذلك فتلف يضمن جميع القيمة لأن الإذن يتناول ما يمثله دون ما لا يسرج بمثله فيكون متعدياً فيضمن، وإن يسرج مثله به لا أسرج بسرج يسرج أ، سواء كان يوكف بمثله أو لا، وهذا قول الإمام. وقالا : الإكاف كالسرج يضمن. وقوله «بما لا يسرج بمثله» قيد بالسرج لا للإكاف لأنه يضمن مطلقاً، مطلقاً لا يضمن إذا كان يوكف بمثله إلا إذا كان زائداً على السرج الذي عليه فيضمن بقدر الزيادة كما في السرج لأنه هو والسرج سواء. والجواب أن الجنس يختلف لأن الإكاف للحمل والسرج للركوب، وكذا ينبسط أحدهما على ظهر الدابة ما لا ينبسط الآخر فصار كاختلاف الحنطة والشعير قال في النهاية : ذكر في الإجارة أنه يضمن بقدر ما زاد وهو قولهما، فمن المشايخ من قال ليس في المسألة روايتان عن الإمام، ومنهم من قال عن الإمام روايتان في رواية يضمن بقدر ما زاد، وفي رواية يضمن جميع القيمة وهو الأصح . وتكلموا في معنى قولهما يضمن بحسابه قال بعضهم إذا كان السرج يأخذ من ظهر الدابة قدر شبرين والإكاف قدر أربعة أشبار فيضمن بحسابه وقيل يعتبر بالوزن. قال قاضيخان : وهذا إذا استأجر الحمار ،مسرجاً، فلو استأجره عرياناً فالمسألة على وجوه : إن استأجره من البلد إلى البلد لا يضمن لأن الحمار لا يركب بينهما إلا بسرج أو إكاف، فإن استأجره ليركب في المصر، فإن كان من ذوات المقامات فكذلك فإنه من عادته أن لا يركب عرياناً، وإن كان من العوام الذين يركبون في المصر عرياناً ففعل يضمن اهـ. أقول : ينبغي أن يقال فيما إذا استأجر من القرية إلى القرية إن كان المستأجر ممن جرت العادة أن يركب من القرية إلى القرية عرياناً كما يشاهد في ديارنا، فإذا أسرجه يضمن وإلا فلا. وفي المحيط : استأجر حماراً بغير لجام فألجمه بلجام مثله لا يضمن لأن اللجام وضع للحفظ فلا بد للراكب منه فيصير مأذوناً للجام دلالة إلا إذا كان الحمار لا يلجم بمثله .اهـ. وفي التتارخانية : ولو هلكت المستأجرة عند المستأجر فاستحقها رجل يضمن المستأجر قيمة ذلك ويرجع على المؤجر كما ضمن اهـ.
He (the author) said: (And removing the saddle and packsaddle, or putting on a saddle that is not like it) meaning if he hired a donkey with a saddle, then removed the saddle and put on a saddle that is not used for such donkeys, or put a packsaddle on it, and it perished, he guarantees the entire value because permission covers what is similar, not what is not similar, so he is a transgressor and guarantees. If he puts a saddle that is similar, no liability whether or not it can bear a packsaddle – this is the view of Imam. The two companions said: The packsaddle is like the saddle, so he guarantees. His statement 'with what is not similar to it' is restricted to the saddle, not the packsaddle, because for the packsaddle he guarantees absolutely. Absolutely he does not guarantee if it can bear such a packsaddle, unless it is in excess of the saddle that was on it, then he guarantees the amount of excess as in the case of the saddle because the packsaddle and saddle are equal. The answer is that the types differ because the packsaddle is for carrying and the saddle for riding, and one spreads on the back of the animal differently from the other, so they are like wheat and barley. In al-Nihayah: He mentioned in Ijarah that he guarantees by the amount of increase – that is the view of the two companions. Some mashayikh said there are no two narrations from Imam in this issue; others said there are two narrations: in one he guarantees by the amount of increase, in another he guarantees the entire value, and that is more correct. They discussed the meaning of 'he guarantees by calculation' – some said if the saddle takes up two spans of the animal's back and the packsaddle four spans, he guarantees proportionally; another said it is based on weight. Qadikhan said: This is if he hired the donkey with a saddle; if he hired it bare, the issue has aspects: if he hired it from city to city, he does not guarantee because the donkey cannot be ridden between them except with a saddle or packsaddle; if he hired it to ride within the city, then if the person is from the distinguished, similarly because it is his custom not to ride bare; if from the commoners who ride bare in the city, and he saddles it, then he guarantees. I (the author) say: Regarding hiring from village to village, if the hirer is one who customarily rides from village to village bare, as seen in our lands, then if he saddles it, he guarantees, otherwise not. In al-Muhit: He hired a donkey without a bridle and put a bridle like it, he does not guarantee because the bridle is for protection, so the rider needs it, and thus permission for the bridle is implied, unless the donkey is not used to being bridled like that. In al-TatarKhaniyyah: If the hired animal perishes in the hirer's possession and then someone claims it, the hirer guarantees the value and recovers from the lessor.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage discusses the liability of a renter who removes the original saddle or packsaddle from a hired donkey and replaces it with a different one. The key point: if he puts on a saddle that is not suitable for that type of donkey (i.e., one that is not customarily used for it), he guarantees the full value because he has exceeded the permission. If he puts on a similar saddle, no liability. However, for a packsaddle (ikaf), the ruling differs: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, putting a packsaddle (even if similar) makes him liable unless the donkey can bear it (i.e., is accustomed to pack saddles). The Sahibayn say that the packsaddle is like the saddle: liability only if it is unsuitable. The text also clarifies that if the donkey was hired bare (without saddle), and the custom of the area dictates that it is ridden bare, then putting a saddle makes him liable. The relied-upon position is that there are two narrations from Imam: one guaranteeing the full value, one guaranteeing the excess, with the latter being the more correct (as in al-Nihayah). The practical consequence is that the renter must ensure that any replacement saddle or packsaddle is appropriate for that particular animal and custom.

Key Terms
السرج (al-sarj): Saddle for riding.
الإكاف (al-ikaf): Packsaddle used for carrying loads.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man hires a donkey with a saddle, removes it, and puts a similar saddle. The donkey dies from a pre-existing condition. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling?
A) He guarantees the full value.
B) He guarantees the cost of the new saddle.
C) He does not guarantee.
D) He guarantees half the value.

Key Takeaway
The type of saddle determines liability: unsuitable riding saddle or any packsaddle (unless animal accustomed) triggers compensation, but the relied-upon view limits it to the excess value.
