Renting for a Year Without Specifying Monthly Rent
Ruling on a rental contract with lump-sum rent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a contract of ijarah for a year with a total rent and explain why it is valid despite missing monthly breakdown.

Core Idea
Total rent and duration known? Contract valid; monthly breakdown not required.

In this passage, the author explains a key Hanafi principle: a rental contract for a year is valid even if the monthly rent is not individually specified, as long as the total rent is stated. This reflects the madhhab's approach to removing uncertainty (gharar) by focusing on overall knowledge rather than minute details.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and the missing term
The contract is ijarah (lease) for one year, but the monthly rent is not specified. The tenant agrees to pay a total sum for the whole year.
2
State the ruling
The ruling is sahih (valid). The Hanafi school holds that the contract is valid because the usufruct (manfa'ah) is known through the fixed duration, and the rent is known through the total amount.
3
Analyze the proof: certainty of terms
The usufruct is known because the duration (one year) is specified. The rent is known because the total is given. This removes fatal uncertainty (gharar fahish) sufficient for validity.
Minor uncertainty in monthly breakdown is tolerated.
4
Determine the consequence of validity
Once the contract is valid, the total rent is divided equally over the months. Seasonal price fluctuations do not affect the distribution.
The division is implicit, not negotiated.
5
Apply the usul principle: qarinat al-hal
The term 'sana' (year) is indefinite (nakirah) but becomes defined by the context of the contract. This shows how contextual evidence clarifies ambiguity.
This supports contract validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وإن استأجرها سنة صح وإن لم يسم أجرة كل شهر) يعني إذا بين الأجرة جملة جاز العقد لأن المنفعة صارت معلومة ببيان المدة والأجرة معلومة وإن لم يبين القسط كل شهر فإذا صح وجب أن يقسم الأجرة على الشهور على السواء، ولا يعتبر تفاوت الأسعار باختلاف الزمان ولما كانت السنة منكرة أفاد أن هذا المنكر يتعين بقرينة الحال .
He said (may Allah have mercy on him): (And if he rents it for a year, it is valid even if he does not specify the rent for each month) meaning, if he states the total rent, the contract is valid because the usufruct becomes known by specifying the period, and the rent is known even if he does not state the installment for each month. So if it is valid, the rent must be divided equally over the months, and the fluctuation of prices over time is not considered. And since the year is indefinite (nakirah), this indicates that this indefinite becomes defined by the contextual evidence (qarinat al-hal).
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage states a clear Hanafi ruling: renting a house for a year with a lump-sum rent (without specifying monthly amounts) is valid. The reason is that the usufruct (manfa'ah) is known by specifying the duration (sana), and the total rent is known. The absence of monthly breakdown does not cause uncertainty (jahalah) because the total is fixed. Once the contract is valid, the total rent is divided equally among the months, regardless of seasonal price fluctuations. This is based on the principle that the term 'sana' (year) is indefinite (nakirah) but becomes defined by context (qarinat al-hal). This ruling reflects the Hanafi prioritization of overall certainty over minute details.

Key Terms
السنة المنكرة (al-sana al-munakkara): An indefinite 'year' that becomes specific due to contextual evidence (qarinat al-hal).
قرينة الحال (qarinat al-hal): Contextual evidence from the circumstances that clarifies an otherwise ambiguous term.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) The market rate for each month applies.

Key Takeaway
A rental contract with a known total rent and duration is valid; monthly breakdown is not required.

The Default Start of the Lease Term in Ijarah
Ruling on the default start of the ijarah term

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi default rule for the start of the lease term in an absolute ijarah contract and explain the rationale using analogy to oaths.

Core Idea
The lease term starts immediately after the contract to avoid uncertainty.

When you rent something without specifying when the lease begins, Hanafi law steps in with a default rule: the term starts right after you sign. This prevents the lease from becoming invalid due to an unknown term. Let's see why it's immediate and how it compares to other areas of fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Locate the explicit statement in the text: the beginning of the period is the time of the contract. Understand that this means immediately after the contract is concluded.
2
Understand the rationale
The text gives a reason: if the start were not immediate, the term would be majhul (unknown), which vitiates the ijarah. This shows the principle that certainty in contractual terms is essential.
3
Apply the analogy (qiyas) with oaths
The text analogizes the contract to an oath (yamin) where a period like 'I will not speak to him for a month' begins immediately. Recognize this as a proof from analogy.
The analogy relies on the common illa of immediate specification.
4
Distinguish the counterexample of fasting
The text notes that in fasting (sawm), the period does not start immediately after an oath or vow because fasting is time-restricted (daytime) and requires intention. Understand why the analogy doesn't hold there.
5
Identify the condition
The rule applies only when the contract is mutlaq (absolute) without a specified start. If a start date is mentioned, that takes precedence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وابتداء المدة وقت العقد) يعني ابتداء أول مدة الإجارة الوقت الذي يلي العقد لأن في مثله يتعين الزمان الذي يلي العقد كالأجل واليمين لا يكلم فلاناً شهراً. ولأنه لو لم يتعين عقيب العقد لصارت مجهولة وبه تبطل الإجارة والظاهر من حالهما أنهما يعقدان العقد الصحيح فتعين عقيب العقد بخلاف الصوم حيث لا يتعين ابتداؤه عقيب اليمين ولا عقيب النذر لأن الأوقاف في حقه ليست سواء فإنه لا يجوز في الليل ولا يصير شارعاً فيه إلا بالعزيمة فلا يتعين عقيب التسبب هذا إذا كان العقد مطلقاً من غير تعيين المدة، وإن بين مدة تعين ذلك وهو ظاهر .
He said (may Allah have mercy on him): (And the beginning of the period is the time of the contract) meaning the beginning of the first period of the ijarah is the time immediately following the contract, because in similar cases the time following the contract becomes specified, like the term in an oath: 'He will not speak to so-and-so for a month.' And because if it were not specified immediately after the contract, it would become unknown (majhul) and thus void the ijarah. The apparent situation is that they make a valid contract, so it becomes specified immediately after the contract, unlike fasting where its beginning is not specified immediately after an oath or vow because the times for it are not equal: it is not valid at night and one only enters it with intention, so it is not specified immediately after the causative action. This [ruling] applies when the contract is absolute without specifying the period; but if a specific period is mentioned, that is specified, which is obvious.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage establishes a default rule for the start of the lease term in an absolute ijarah contract. The rule: unless the parties explicitly specify a start date, the lease term begins immediately after the contract is concluded. The reason is that if it were not immediately definite, the term would become unknown (majhul), invalidating the ijarah. This is analogous to an oath (yamin) where the period starts immediately. The commentator contrasts this with fasting (sawm), where the start time is not automatically set after an oath or vow because fasting has specific permissible times (daylight) and requires intention (niyyah). The rule holds when the contract is mutlaq (absolute) without a specified period; if a period is mentioned, that takes precedence.

Key Terms
المدة (al-muddah): The period or term of the lease, which begins immediately after the contract if not specified.
اليمين (al-yamin): An oath; used as analogy to show immediate specification of time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under Hanafi law, if a lease contract is made without specifying when it begins, when does the lease term start?
A) The next day after the contract.
B) Immediately after the contract is concluded.
C) At the beginning of the next month.
D) The lease is void because the period is unknown.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the lease term in an absolute ijarah contract begins immediately after the contract to avoid uncertainty.

Calculating Lease Period by Lunar Months or Days
Ruling on calculation of lease period based on start time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule for calculating lease duration in a Hanafi ijara contract and apply it to determine the end date based on the start time.

Core Idea
Lease term: lunar months if start coincides with new moon; otherwise 30-day months.

When entering into a lease (ijara), the duration must be clearly defined. Islamic law uses the lunar calendar, but not all lease periods start at the beginning of a lunar month. The Hanafi school provides a practical rule to resolve this: if the lease begins exactly when the new moon is sighted, count by lunar months; otherwise, count each month as 30 days. This lesson unpacks that rule and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the start condition
Determine whether the lease commencement coincides with the sighting of the new moon (halla).
If the lease starts exactly at the moment of the new moon, the condition is met; otherwise, it is not.
2
Apply the appropriate calculation
If condition is met, count months by lunar months (from one new moon to the next). If not, count each month as 30 days.
Lunar months vary between 29 and 30 days, so the total duration may differ from a fixed 30-day month count.
3
Understand the practical effect
Recognize that a lunar year is about 354 days, whereas a 30-day month year is exactly 360 days for 12 months.
This rule ensures clarity and avoids disputes over the exact end date.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (فإن كان حين يهل يعتبر بالأهلة وإلا فالأيام)
He said (may Allah have mercy on him): (For if it is at the time of the sighting of the new moon, it is considered by lunar months; otherwise, by days.)
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This is a concise rule from the matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) regarding the calculation of the lease period. If the lease begins at the sighting of the new moon (halla), then the months are counted by lunar months (i.e., from one new moon to the next). If it does not start at a new moon, then the period is calculated by days (30 days per month usually). This affects the actual duration of the lease. The commentator likely expands on this with examples, but the text cuts off. This is a standard Hanafi position to handle the discrepancy between lunar and solar months.

Key Terms
الأهلة (al-ahillah): Lunar months based on sighting of the new moon; used when lease starts at new moon.
الأيام (al-ayyam): Days (30-day months) used when the lease does not start at a new moon.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a lease is agreed upon to start on the first day of the lunar month (new moon), how is the period calculated?
A) By lunar months (based on sighting of the new moon).
B) By 30-day months regardless.
C) By solar months.
D) By the Gregorian calendar.

Key Takeaway
The duration of a lease is calculated either by lunar months or 30-day months depending on whether the lease starts at the sighting of the new moon.

Validity of Hire (Ijarah) Without Specifying Monthly Rent
Establishes ruling on hire contract validity when total rent is known but monthly share unspecified

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of an ijarah contract when the monthly rent is unspecified, explain the basis for the option to dissolve, and identify the mufta bihi position regarding the timing of the option.

Core Idea
A hire contract is valid if total rent and term are known; ignorance of the monthly breakdown does not invalidate.

In Hanafi contract law, uncertainty (jahalah) can invalidate a contract if it leads to dispute. However, when the total rent and the duration are specified, the monthly breakdown is not essential. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies this principle and also addresses the parties' right to cancel at the beginning of each month. You will learn the ruling, the reasoning behind it, and the internal Hanafi difference on when the option applies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (ijarah for a year without specifying monthly rent) and the hukm level (sahih - valid).
The text explicitly states: 'استأجرها سنة صح وإن لم يسم أجرة كل شهر'.
2
Locate the proof
Identify the evidence for the ruling. The proof is aqli (rational): because the total benefit and rent are known, the uncertainty is tolerable. The text also cites an analogy to the ruling on oaths (istihsan).
Argument type is dalil aqli, not a direct Quran/Hadith quote.
3
Trace the reasoning for validity
Explain why the contract is valid despite unspecified monthly rent: the benefit (manfa'ah) is known from the total term, and the total rent is known. Jahalah (ignorance) that does not lead to dispute is tolerated.
The rent is divided equally over the months regardless of seasonal price differences.
4
Identify the option to dissolve (khiyar al-faskh)
According to zahir al-riwayah, each party has the option to cancel at the first night and day of each month. The text defines 'beginning of the month' as the first night and day based on Muhammad al-Shaybani's ruling on oaths.
The fatwa is on this position (wa bihi yufata).
5
Note the internal Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some scholars (in al-Muhit) hold that the option only arises from the second month. Understand the basis of each view and the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference).
Tarjih: The mufta bihi is the zahir riwayah view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
استأجرها سنة صح وإن لم يسم أجرة كل شهر وابتداء المدة وقت العقد فإن كان حين الفساد كذا في النهاية مختصراً. وظاهر الرواية أن لكل واحد منهما الخيار في الليلة الأولى ويومها وبه يفتى، لأن في اعتبار الساعات حرجاً بيناً، والمقصود هو الفسخ في رأس الشهر وهو عبارة عن اليلة الأولى ويومها لأن محمداً قال : لو حلف ليقضي فلاناً دينه في رأس الشهر فقضاه في الليلة التي يهل فيها الهلال ويومها لم يحنث استحساناً. وظاهر قوله صح في شهر واحد في الباقي كما تقدم . قال في المحيط : وهذا قول بعضهم والصحيح أن الإجارة كل شهر جائزة، وإطلاق محمد يدل على هذا فيجوز العقد في الشهر الأول والثاني والثالث . وإنما يثبت خيار الفسخ لكل واحد منهما في أول الشهر الثاني لأن الإجارة في الشهر الثاني مضافة إلى وقت في المستقبل، ولكن واحد فسخ الإجارة المضافة إلى وقت في المستقبل. وقوله «داراً» مثال لأنه لو استأجر ثوراً ليطحن عليه كل يوم بدرهم فالحكم كذلك. قال رحمه الله : (وكل شهر سكن ساعة منه صح فيه لأنه صار معلوماً فتتم العقد فيه بتراضيهما وهو قول بعض المشايخ وهو القياس. وعلى ما في الأصل إذا سكن يوماً أو يومين صح وليس لواحد منهما الفسخ وهو ظاهر الرواية على ما قدمنا ولو قدم أجرة شهر أو أكثر وقبض المعجل يوماً لا يكون لكل واحد منهما الفسخ فيما عجل لأن بالتقديم زالت الجهالة في ذلك القدر فصار كالمسمى في العقد قال في المحيط : الإجارة الطويلة التي تفعل ببخارى صورتها أنهم يؤجرون الدار والأرض سنين مدة معلومة متوالية غير ثلاثة أيام في آخر كل سنة على أن كلا منهما بالخيار في ثلاثة أيام من آخر كل سنة ويجعلون لكل سنة أجرة قليلة ويجعلون بقية الأجرة للسنة الأخيرة؛ الصحيح أن هذا العقد جائز لأن هذا ليس بشرط الخيار في الإجارة بل استثناء ثلاثة أيام. قال رحمه الله : (وإن استأجرها سنة صح وإن لم يسم أجرة كل شهر) يعني إذا بين الأجرة جملة جاز العقد لأن المنفعة صارت معلومة ببيان المدة والأجرة معلومة وإن لم يبين القسط كل شهر فإذا صح وجب أن يقسم الأجرة على الشهور على السواء، ولا يعتبر تفاوت الأسعار باختلاف الزمان ولما كانت السنة منكرة أفاد أن هذا المنكر يتعين بقرينة الحال . قال رحمه الله : ( وابتداء المدة وقت العقد) يعني ابتداء أول مدة الإجارة الوقت الذي يلي العقد لأن في مثله يتعين الزمان الذي يلي العقد كالأجل واليمين لا يكلم فلاناً شهراً. ولأنه لو لم يتعين عقيب العقد لصارت مجهولة وبه تبطل الإجارة والظاهر من حالهما أنهما يعقدان العقد الصحيح فتعين عقيب العقد بخلاف الصوم حيث لا يتعين ابتداؤه عقيب اليمين ولا عقيب النذر لأن الأوقاف في حقه ليست سواء فإنه لا يجوز في الليل ولا يصير شارعاً فيه إلا بالعزيمة فلا يتعين عقيب التسبب هذا إذا كان العقد مطلقاً من غير تعيين المدة، وإن بين مدة تعين ذلك وهو ظاهر .
If he hires it for a year, it is valid even if he did not name the rent of each month, and the beginning of the term is at the time of the contract. Then if (the contract is) at the time of the new moon? So in al-Nihayah briefly. The apparent riwayah is that each of them has the option in the first night and its day, and this is the fatwa, because considering hours is manifestly burdensome, and the intended object is dissolution at the beginning of the month, which is the first night and its day because Muhammad said: If he swore to pay someone his debt at the beginning of the month and he paid it in the night when the new moon appears and its day, he does not break the oath by istihsan. And the apparent meaning of his saying 'valid' is in one month in the remaining as previously. He said in al-Muhit: This is the statement of some of them, and the correct view is that the hiring each month is permissible, and the absolute statement of Muhammad indicates this, so the contract is valid in the first, second, and third months. The option of dissolution is only established for each of them at the beginning of the second month because the hiring in the second month is added to a future time, but one dissolves the hiring added to a future time. And his saying 'a house' is an example because if he hired a bull to grind with it every day for a dirham, the ruling is the same. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And every month he dwells an hour of it is valid therein because it becomes known, so the contract is completed in it by their mutual consent, and this is the statement of some shaykhs, and it is the qiyas. And according to what is in al-Asl, if he dwells a day or two days, it is valid and neither of them has the option to dissolve, and this is the apparent riwayah as we have presented. And if he paid the rent of a month or more in advance and took the accelerated payment a day, neither of them has the option to dissolve regarding what was advanced because by advancing the ignorance in that amount is removed, so it becomes like the named in the contract. He said in al-Muhit: The long-term hiring practiced in Bukhara: its form is that they lease a house and land for a known number of consecutive years, except three days at the end of each year, contingent on each of them having the option in three days of the end of each year, and they assign a small rent for each year and assign the rest of the rent for the last year. The correct view is that this contract is permissible because this is not a condition of option in hiring but an exception of three days. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And if he hires it for a year, it is valid even if he did not name the rent of each month' – meaning when he specifies the total rent, the contract is permissible because the benefit is known by specifying the period and the rent is known even if he does not specify the installment for each month. When it is valid, the rent must be divided equally over the months, and the variation of prices due to differing times is not considered. And since 'year' is indefinite, this indicates that this indefinite is specified by contextual indication. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And the beginning of the term is at the time of the contract' – meaning the beginning of the first period of the hiring is the time immediately following the contract, because in similar cases the time immediately following the contract is determined, like the term and the oath 'he will not speak to so-and-so for a month.' And because if it were not determined immediately after the contract, it would become unknown, and thereby the hire would be invalid. The apparent situation is that they make a valid contract, so it is determined immediately after the contract, unlike fasting where its beginning is not determined immediately after the oath or after the vow because the times are not equal in his regard – it is not valid at night and he does not enter into it except by intention, so it is not determined immediately after the causative act. This is when the contract is absolute without specification of the period. If he specifies a period, that is determined, and it is apparent.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a ruling explanation from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a Hanafi commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It addresses the validity of an ijarah (hire) contract when the parties agree on a total rent for a year without specifying the monthly amount. The author confirms that the contract is valid (sahih) because the benefit (manfa'ah) is known by specifying the total term and total rent, and ignorance of the monthly breakdown does not cause invalidity. The rent is then divided equally over the months regardless of seasonal price differences. The beginning of the term is immediately after the contract (waqt al-'aqd), analogous to the start of an oath or a fixed term. If the term is absolute, it starts right after the contract; if a specific start date is mentioned, that governs. The text then discusses the option to dissolve (khiyar al-faskh) at the beginning of each month. According to the 'zahir al-riwayah', each party has the option to cancel in the first night and day of each month. This is the view given for fatwa because counting hours is burdensome. The beginning of the month (ra's al-shahr) is defined as the first night and day, based on Muhammad al-Shaybani's ruling on oaths. There is an internal Hanafi difference: some say the option exists only from the second month onwards because the first month's hire is immediate, not future. But the more accepted view is that the contract is valid month by month, and the option exists at the start of each month, including the first. The text also considers the case where rent is paid in advance for a month or more: if paid early, the option to dissolve that portion ceases because the ignorance is removed. Finally, it mentions a common practice in Bukhara where a long-term lease includes a three-day break each year with a small annual rent and a large final payment; this is judged permissible because it is not a condition of option but a genuine exclusion of three days.

Key Terms
خيار الفسخ (khiyar al-faskh): The option to annul or dissolve the contract unilaterally at specified times.
جهالة (jahalah): Ignorance or uncertainty about essential terms of the contract, which can render it invalid if excessive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the term of a hire contract begin if no specific start date is mentioned?
A) At the beginning of the next month
B) Immediately after the contract
C) At the end of the contract signing
D) After one month from the contract

Key Takeaway
A hire contract is valid even without specifying monthly rent, as long as total rent and term are known; the parties have the option to dissolve at the beginning of each month.

Calculating Months in Hire: Abu Hanifa vs. Muhammad al-Shaybani
Intra-Hanafi dispute on month calculation in ijara

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi views on calculating months in a hire contract and apply the ruling when a contract is made after the month has started.

Core Idea
If a hire contract begins mid-month, Abu Hanifa counts all months as 30 days; Muhammad adjusts first and last months only.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi dispute on how to count months in a hire contract when the start date is not at the new moon. The disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani hinges on consistency versus practicality. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply legal reasoning to analogous cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the trigger condition
Determine whether the contract is made at the time of the new moon or after some part of the month has passed. The rule changes accordingly.
If at new moon, lunar months are used; if not, a dispute arises.
2
State Abu Hanifa's rule
When the contract is made after the month has started, each month is considered as 30 days for the entire term.
This is the view of the Imam and a riwayah from Abu Yusuf.
3
State Muhammad's rule
Only the first month is counted by the remaining days, and the last month is completed by days; the middle months remain as lunar months.
Muhammad tries to preserve the lunar nature of months.
4
Analyze the reasoning
Abu Hanifa argues that if the first month cannot be based on lunar sightings, consistency demands the same for all months. Muhammad argues that the middle months are independent and should remain lunar.
Each imam uses a different principle: consistency vs. preservation of the original rule.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is the total number of days in the contract term, affecting the end date and rental obligations.
Under Abu Hanifa, a one-year contract = 360 days; under Muhammad, it varies based on actual lunar months.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن كان حين يهل يعتبر بالأهلة وإلا فالأيام قال صاحب النهاية : بضم الياء وفتح الهاء على صيغة البناء للمفعول أي يبصر الهلال وقال : أراد به اليوم الأول اهـ. قال ابن قاضي زاده وليس المراد بقوله اليوم الأول تفسير معنى حين يهل إذ قد علم معناه من التفسير السابق قطعاً بل مراده بذلك بيان أثر قوله حين يهل. وليس المراد معناه الحقيقي بل المراد معناه العرفي وهو اليوم الأول من الشهر اهـ. يعني إذا وقع عقد الإجارة في ليلة الهلال أو في يومها تعتبر المدة بالأهلة، وإن كان بعدما مضي شيء من الشهر يعتبر بالأيام وهو أن يعتبر كل شهر ثلاثون يوماً وهذا قول الإمام وهو رواية عن الثاني. وقال محمد : يعتبر الأول بالأيام ويكمل من الأخير ويبقى غيره على الأصل، وللإمام أنه لما تعذر اعتبار الشهر الأول بالأهلة فكذا البقية .اهـ. قال رحمه الله : (وصح أخذ أجرة الحمام) لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم ما رآه المؤمنون حسناً فهو عند الله حسن» (۱) قال الأكمل: وإنما ذكر هذه في ا الفاسدة أنها جائزة لأن بعض العلماء خالف في ذلك قال الشارح : وبعض العلماء كره الحمام لما روي عنه عليه الصلاة والسلام أنه سماه شر بيت. وقال عثمان : إنه بيت العلماء الشيطان. ومن من كرهه للنساء لا للرجال والصحيح أنه لا بأس بالحمامات للرجال والنساء وفي الخلاصة : استأجر حماماً في قرية فوقع الجلاء في القرية ونفر الناس سقطت الأجرة، أو نفر بعض الناس لا تسقط. وفي المحيط : إذا كان حمام للرجال وحمام للنساء فأجرهما جميعاً. حماماً جاز استحساناً إذا كان باب الحمامين واحداً، وإن كان لكل واحد وسمي باب على حدة لا يجوز العقد .اهـ. وفي الخلاصة : استأجر حماماً ببدل على أن عليه الأجرة حال جريان الماء وانقطاعه فالإجارة فاسدة. وفي الخانية شيل الرماد والسرقين وتفريغ موضع البالوغة وغيرها على المستأجر فإن شرط على المؤجر فسدت .اهـ. وقال في المحيط : ولو امتلأ مسيل ماء الحمام فعلى المستأجر تفريغه ولو امتلأت البالوعة فعلى الآجر تفريغها، والفرق أن تفريغ مسيل الماء يمكن من غير نقض البناء، وأما البالوعة فلا يمكن تفريغها بنفسه إلا بنقض شيء من البناء ولا يملك المستأجر نقض شيء من البناء وإنما يلكه رب الأرض فجعل تفريغه عليه . وفيه أيضاً : استأجر حمامين سنة فانهدم أحدهما قبل القبض فله ترك الباقي لأن الصفقة تفرقت عليه قبل التمام بخلاف ما لو استأجر حماماً سنة فلم يسلمه إلى المستأجر حتى مضى شهران ولم ينتفع وامتنع المستأجر من القبض فإنه يجبر على القبض ولا يخير لأن الصفقة هنا تفرقت في حق المنافع فلا يوجب ثبوت الخيار وهناك في القبض، وإذا انهدم الحمام قبل القبض فله الخيار ولو انهدم أحد الحمامين بعد القبض فالباقي لازم بحصته لأن الصفقة تفرقت بعد التمام استأجر حماماً وعبداً ليقوم عليه فانهدم الحمام بعد قبضهما فله
Then if (the contract is) at the time when the new moon is visible, it is considered by the lunar months; otherwise by days. The author of al-Nihayah said: With damma on the ya and fatha on the ha, passive form, i.e., the new moon is seen. He said: He meant by it the first day. Ibn Qadi Zada said: He did not mean by 'first day' an interpretation of the meaning of 'when it appears' since its meaning is certainly known from the previous interpretation, but rather he intended by that to explain the effect of his saying 'when it appears'. He did not mean its real meaning but its customary meaning, which is the first day of the month. That is, if the hire contract occurs on the night of the new moon or its day, the term is considered by lunar months; if after some part of the month has passed, it is considered by days, i.e., each month is considered thirty days. This is the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa and a riwayah from Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: The first month is considered by days and the last is completed from it, and the rest remain on the original basis. Imam argued: since it is impossible to consider the first month by lunar months, so also the rest. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And it is valid to take the wage of the bathhouse (hammam)' due to his saying, peace be upon him, 'What the believers see as good is good in the sight of Allah.' [Ahmad, Musnad 1/379] Al-Akmal said: He mentioned this in the chapter of invalid hire to show that it is permissible because some scholars differed on it. The commentator said: Some scholars disliked the bathhouse due to what was narrated from him, peace be upon him, that he called it the worst house. And 'Uthman said: It is the house of the scholars of the Devil. Some disliked it for women, not for men. The correct view is that there is no harm in bathhouses for men and women. In al-Khulasa: If he hired a bathhouse in a village and a plague occurred in the village and people fled, the rent is dropped; if some people fled, it does not drop. In al-Muhit: If there is a bathhouse for men and a bathhouse for women, and he hired both together, it is permissible by istihsan if the door of the two bathhouses is one; if each has a separate named door, the contract is not permissible. In al-Khulasa: If he hired a bathhouse for a payment on condition that the rent is due whether water flows or stops, the hire is invalid. In al-Khaniyya: Removing ash, dung, and emptying the cesspool, etc., is on the lessee; if he stipulates it on the lessor, the hire becomes invalid. And he said in al-Muhit: If the water channel of the bathhouse becomes full, the lessee must clear it; if the cesspool becomes full, the lessor must clear it. The difference is that clearing the water channel is possible without demolishing the building, while the cesspool cannot be cleared without demolishing some of the building, and the lessee does not have the right to demolish any part of the building; only the owner does, so its clearing is placed on him. Therein also: If he hired two bathhouses for a year and one collapsed before taking possession, he has the right to leave the remaining because the transaction is split before completion, unlike if he hired one bathhouse for a year and the lessor did not hand it over until two months passed without the lessee using it and the lessee refused to take possession – then he is forced to take possession and does not have the option, because here the transaction is split in terms of benefits, which does not establish the option, while there it is in terms of possession. If the bathhouse collapses before taking possession, he has the option. If one of two bathhouses collapses after taking possession, the remaining is binding for its share because the transaction split after completion.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage continues Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq's commentary on the chapter of invalid hire. It first explains the calculation of months in a hire contract. If the contract is made on the night or day of the new moon, the months are counted by actual lunar sightings (ahillah). If the contract is made after some days of the month have passed, months are counted as thirty days each. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa and one riwayah from Abu Yusuf. Muhammad al-Shaybani holds a different view: the first month is counted by days (the remaining days of that month) and the last month is similarly adjusted, while the middle months remain as lunar months. Abu Hanifa's argument is that if it is impossible to count the first month by lunar sightings (because the month is already partially gone), then the same applies to all subsequent months for consistency. The passage then moves to the ruling on taking wages for a bathhouse (hammam) and cupping (hijamah). It states that taking wages for a bathhouse is valid, based on the general principle that 'what the believers consider good is good with Allah.' This is mentioned in the chapter of invalid hire because some scholars considered it disliked. The correct Hanafi position is that there is no harm in bathhouses for either men or women, though some disliked them for women. Various practical issues follow: if the village suffers a plague and people flee, the rent drops; if only some flee, it does not. If a bathhouse is hired and the lessee fails to take possession, he is forced to take it and has no option, unlike the case of physical destruction before possession. Special rules apply when hiring two bathhouses: if they have a common entrance, the contract can be valid by istihsan; if separate entrances, it is invalid due to uncertainty. Duties like cleaning ash, dung, and emptying cesspools are generally on the lessee, but if specified on the lessor, the contract becomes invalid. The water channel (masil) must be cleared by the lessee, while the cesspool (balu'ah) must be cleared by the lessor because clearing the latter requires damaging the building, which only the owner can do. The passage concludes with cases of destruction: if one of two hired bathhouses collapses before possession, the lessee may cancel the remaining; if after possession, the remaining is binding with reduced rent proportionate to the lost part.

Key Terms
أهلة (ahillah): Lunar months, based on the sighting of the new moon.
أيام (ayyam): Days used as a substitute when lunar months cannot be applied.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a hire contract is made on the 15th of a month, according to Abu Hanifa, how many days are in each month of the contract?
A) 29 or 30 depending on lunar
B) 30 days
C) Only the first month is 30
D) Depends on the month

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a hire contract does not start at the new moon, month calculation becomes a matter of ijtihad between standardization (Abu Hanifa) and preservation of lunar months (Muhammad).

Ruling on Bathhouse Wages and Conditions for a Valid Hire Contract
Ruling with proof on bathhouse wages and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on taking wages for a bathhouse and identify the conditions that affect the validity of the hire contract, including maintenance responsibilities and entrance configurations.

Core Idea
Taking wages for a bathhouse is permissible by default; special conditions like separate entrances can invalidate the contract.

This lesson covers the permissibility of hiring out a bathhouse, a practice debated among early scholars. The Hanafi school relies on the general principle that what the community deems good is acceptable, while also detailing practical conditions for a valid contract. You will learn the proof from hadith and the detailed rulings on maintenance, entrances, and destruction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
The text states that it is valid to take wages for a bathhouse, contrasting with some scholars who disliked it.
The ruling is mentioned in the chapter of invalid hire to indicate permissibility.
2
Recognize the hadith proof
The hadith 'What the believers see as good is good with Allah' is cited as a proof for the permissibility of bathhouse wages.
This is a general principle for matters not explicitly addressed in revelation.
3
Note the disagreement
Some scholars disliked bathhouses, especially for women; the correct Hanafi view is that there is no harm for men or women.
The hadith is used to override the negative narrations about bathhouses.
4
List the conditions for validity
The contract is invalid if the bathhouse has separate named doors for men and women; it is valid if there is one common entrance. Also, stipulating that the lessor does routine cleaning (e.g., removing ash) invalidates the contract.
Separate doors create uncertainty (gharar) about which part is hired.
5
Determine maintenance responsibilities
The lessee must clear water channels and remove ash/dung, but the lessor must empty cesspools because that requires structural demolition.
The distinction is based on whether the task can be done without damaging the building.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن كان حين يهل يعتبر بالأهلة وإلا فالأيام قال صاحب النهاية : بضم الياء وفتح الهاء على صيغة البناء للمفعول أي يبصر الهلال وقال : أراد به اليوم الأول اهـ. قال ابن قاضي زاده وليس المراد بقوله اليوم الأول تفسير معنى حين يهل إذ قد علم معناه من التفسير السابق قطعاً بل مراده بذلك بيان أثر قوله حين يهل. وليس المراد معناه الحقيقي بل المراد معناه العرفي وهو اليوم الأول من الشهر اهـ. يعني إذا وقع عقد الإجارة في ليلة الهلال أو في يومها تعتبر المدة بالأهلة، وإن كان بعدما مضي شيء من الشهر يعتبر بالأيام وهو أن يعتبر كل شهر ثلاثون يوماً وهذا قول الإمام وهو رواية عن الثاني. وقال محمد : يعتبر الأول بالأيام ويكمل من الأخير ويبقى غيره على الأصل، وللإمام أنه لما تعذر اعتبار الشهر الأول بالأهلة فكذا البقية .اهـ. قال رحمه الله : (وصح أخذ أجرة الحمام) لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم ما رآه المؤمنون حسناً فهو عند الله حسن» (۱) قال الأكمل: وإنما ذكر هذه في ا الفاسدة أنها جائزة لأن بعض العلماء خالف في ذلك قال الشارح : وبعض العلماء كره الحمام لما روي عنه عليه الصلاة والسلام أنه سماه شر بيت. وقال عثمان : إنه بيت العلماء الشيطان. ومن من كرهه للنساء لا للرجال والصحيح أنه لا بأس بالحمامات للرجال والنساء وفي الخلاصة : استأجر حماماً في قرية فوقع الجلاء في القرية ونفر الناس سقطت الأجرة، أو نفر بعض الناس لا تسقط. وفي المحيط : إذا كان حمام للرجال وحمام للنساء فأجرهما جميعاً. حماماً جاز استحساناً إذا كان باب الحمامين واحداً، وإن كان لكل واحد وسمي باب على حدة لا يجوز العقد .اهـ. وفي الخلاصة : استأجر حماماً ببدل على أن عليه الأجرة حال جريان الماء وانقطاعه فالإجارة فاسدة. وفي الخانية شيل الرماد والسرقين وتفريغ موضع البالوغة وغيرها على المستأجر فإن شرط على المؤجر فسدت .اهـ. وقال في المحيط : ولو امتلأ مسيل ماء الحمام فعلى المستأجر تفريغه ولو امتلأت البالوعة فعلى الآجر تفريغها، والفرق أن تفريغ مسيل الماء يمكن من غير نقض البناء، وأما البالوعة فلا يمكن تفريغها بنفسه إلا بنقض شيء من البناء ولا يملك المستأجر نقض شيء من البناء وإنما يلكه رب الأرض فجعل تفريغه عليه . وفيه أيضاً : استأجر حمامين سنة فانهدم أحدهما قبل القبض فله ترك الباقي لأن الصفقة تفرقت عليه قبل التمام بخلاف ما لو استأجر حماماً سنة فلم يسلمه إلى المستأجر حتى مضى شهران ولم ينتفع وامتنع المستأجر من القبض فإنه يجبر على القبض ولا يخير لأن الصفقة هنا تفرقت في حق المنافع فلا يوجب ثبوت الخيار وهناك في القبض، وإذا انهدم الحمام قبل القبض فله الخيار ولو انهدم أحد الحمامين بعد القبض فالباقي لازم بحصته لأن الصفقة تفرقت بعد التمام استأجر حماماً وعبداً ليقوم عليه فانهدم الحمام بعد قبضهما فله
Then if (the contract is) at the time when the new moon is visible, it is considered by the lunar months; otherwise by days. The author of al-Nihayah said: With damma on the ya and fatha on the ha, passive form, i.e., the new moon is seen. He said: He meant by it the first day. Ibn Qadi Zada said: He did not mean by 'first day' an interpretation of the meaning of 'when it appears' since its meaning is certainly known from the previous interpretation, but rather he intended by that to explain the effect of his saying 'when it appears'. He did not mean its real meaning but its customary meaning, which is the first day of the month. That is, if the hire contract occurs on the night of the new moon or its day, the term is considered by lunar months; if after some part of the month has passed, it is considered by days, i.e., each month is considered thirty days. This is the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa and a riwayah from Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: The first month is considered by days and the last is completed from it, and the rest remain on the original basis. Imam argued: since it is impossible to consider the first month by lunar months, so also the rest. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And it is valid to take the wage of the bathhouse (hammam)' due to his saying, peace be upon him, 'What the believers see as good is good in the sight of Allah.' [Ahmad, Musnad 1/379] Al-Akmal said: He mentioned this in the chapter of invalid hire to show that it is permissible because some scholars differed on it. The commentator said: Some scholars disliked the bathhouse due to what was narrated from him, peace be upon him, that he called it the worst house. And 'Uthman said: It is the house of the scholars of the Devil. Some disliked it for women, not for men. The correct view is that there is no harm in bathhouses for men and women. In al-Khulasa: If he hired a bathhouse in a village and a plague occurred in the village and people fled, the rent is dropped; if some people fled, it does not drop. In al-Muhit: If there is a bathhouse for men and a bathhouse for women, and he hired both together, it is permissible by istihsan if the door of the two bathhouses is one; if each has a separate named door, the contract is not permissible. In al-Khulasa: If he hired a bathhouse for a payment on condition that the rent is due whether water flows or stops, the hire is invalid. In al-Khaniyya: Removing ash, dung, and emptying the cesspool, etc., is on the lessee; if he stipulates it on the lessor, the hire becomes invalid. And he said in al-Muhit: If the water channel of the bathhouse becomes full, the lessee must clear it; if the cesspool becomes full, the lessor must clear it. The difference is that clearing the water channel is possible without demolishing the building, while the cesspool cannot be cleared without demolishing some of the building, and the lessee does not have the right to demolish any part of the building; only the owner does, so its clearing is placed on him. Therein also: If he hired two bathhouses for a year and one collapsed before taking possession, he has the right to leave the remaining because the transaction is split before completion, unlike if he hired one bathhouse for a year and the lessor did not hand it over until two months passed without the lessee using it and the lessee refused to take possession – then he is forced to take possession and does not have the option, because here the transaction is split in terms of benefits, which does not establish the option, while there it is in terms of possession. If the bathhouse collapses before taking possession, he has the option. If one of two bathhouses collapses after taking possession, the remaining is binding for its share because the transaction split after completion.

Key Terms
الحمام (al-hammam): A public bathhouse, which may be hired for use or operated as a business.
بالوعة (balu'ah): Cesspool or pit for wastewater in a bathhouse, whose emptying is the owner's responsibility if it requires building demolition.

Determining the Ijarah Term: Moons or Days?
Expansion on ijarah term calculation with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ijarah term calculation when the contract starts mid-month and explain the intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
If the ijarah contract starts after the crescent, each month counts as thirty days.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on a brief matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq about ijarah term calculation. The core question: how do we count months when the contract begins after the month has started? The Hanafi school splits between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani. This lesson walks through their arguments and the practical difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base matn ruling
The matn says: 'It is considered by the moons, otherwise by days.' Understand that this is the default rule.
2
Understand when moons apply
If the ijarah contract is made on the night or day of the crescent (first day), the term uses actual lunar months.
3
Understand when days apply
If the contract is made after the crescent has passed, each month is treated as thirty days. This is Abu Hanifa's position.
4
Contrast Muhammad's position
Muhammad al-Shaybani says the first month is counted by remaining days, the last month completed, and intermediate months on the lunar basis.
The difference leads to different end dates for the same contract.
5
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
His reasoning is qiyas jali: since the first month cannot be determined by moons, the same applies to all subsequent months.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يهل يعتبر بالأهلة وإلا فالأيام . صاحب النهاية : بضم الياء وفتح الهاء على صيغة البناء للمفعول أي يبصر الهلال وقال : أراد به اليوم الأول اهـ. قال ابن قاضي زاده : وليس المراد بقوله اليوم الأول تفسير معنى حين يهل إذ قد علم معناه من التفسير السابق قطعاً بل مراده بذلك بيان أثر قوله حين يهل. وليس المراد معناه الحقيقي بل المراد معناه العرفي وهو اليوم الأول من الشهر اهـ. يعني إذا وقع عقد الإجارة في ليلة الهلال أو في يومها تعتبر المدة بالأهلة، وإن كان بعدما مضي شيء من الشهر يعتبر بالأيام وهو أن يعتبر كل شهر ثلاثون يوماً وهذا قول الإمام وهو رواية عن الثاني. وقال محمد : يعتبر الأول بالأيام ويكمل من الأخير ويبقى غيره على الأصل، وللإمام أنه لما تعذر اعتبار الشهر الأول بالأهلة فكذا البقية .اهـ.
It is considered by the moons, otherwise by days. The author of al-Nihayah: with damma on the ya and fatha on the ha on the passive construction meaning the crescent is seen, and he said: he meant by it the first day. Ibn Qadi Zada said: His saying 'the first day' is not intended to interpret the meaning of 'when it appears' as its meaning is already known from the previous interpretation, but rather his aim is to clarify the effect of his saying 'when it appears'. And the intended meaning is not the literal but the customary meaning, which is the first day of the month. That is, if the contract of ijarah occurs on the night of the crescent or on its day, the term is considered by moons; if after some days of the month have passed, it is considered by days, that is, each month is counted as thirty days. This is the saying of the Imam (Abu Hanifa) and it is a narration from the second (Abu Yusuf). Muhammad said: the first is counted by days, and the last is completed, and the rest remains on the original. According to the Imam, since considering the first month by moons is not possible, likewise the rest.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage expands the matn ruling on how to determine the term of an ijarah contract when expressed in months. The matn states: 'It is considered by the moons, otherwise by days.' The commentator explains the parsing and clarifies that the customary meaning of 'when it appears' is the first day of the lunar month. If the contract is made on the night or day the crescent is sighted, the entire term uses actual lunar months. If made after some days pass, each month is treated as 30 days. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa, also narrated from Abu Yusuf. Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that the first month is counted by days (the remainder) and the last month is completed, while intermediate months remain on the lunar basis. Abu Hanifa's reasoning is that since the first month cannot be determined by moons, the same applies to all subsequent months.

Key Terms
يهل (yuhillu): The crescent moon appears; marks the beginning of a lunar month.
الأهلة (al-ahillah): Plural of hilal, the crescent moons used to measure lunar months.
الإجارة الفاسدة (al-ijarah al-fasidah): A hire contract that is defective in its conditions but may still have some legal effects.
البناء للمفعول (al-bina' li al-maf'ul): The passive voice construction in Arabic grammar.
العرفي (al-'urfi): Customary meaning, as opposed to literal (haqiqi).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
When an ijarah contract begins after the crescent, the mufta bihi view (Abu Hanifa) counts each month as thirty days for the entire term.

Permissibility of Wages for Hiring a Bathhouse (Hammam)
Ruling on bathhouse wages with subrulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wages for hiring a bathhouse, identify the proof from hadith, and apply the subrulings on conditions that affect the validity of the ijarah.

Core Idea
What Muslims customarily deem good is good with Allah; thus bathhouse wages are permissible despite impurities.

The Hanafi school validates taking wages for hiring a bathhouse (hammam), supporting this with the prophetic tradition that 'what Muslims see as good is good with Allah.' This lesson unpacks the main ruling, the proof, and a range of subsidiary issues that arise in such contracts, from plague-induced vacancy to the allocation of cleaning duties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
The matn states that taking wages for the bathhouse is valid. The author cites the hadith about Muslim consensus as the proof.
This hadith is considered a basis for istihsan.
2
Examine the proof's legal force
Analyze how the hadith 'ما رآه المؤمنون حسناً فهو عند الله حسن' supports permissibility: continuous Muslim practice establishes a precedent.
The hadith is zanni in both transmission and meaning.
3
Note the historical difference of opinion
Some early scholars disliked the bathhouse; the correct view (as per the commentator) is permissibility for both men and women.
The dislike was due to reported statements, but they are overridden by the stronger proof of custom.
4
Apply the subrulings on conditions
Work through the text's examples: hiring with improper conditions (e.g., paying whether water flows) renders the ijarah fasid; separate doors invalidate the contract; cleaning duties depend on whether demolition is needed.
These subrulings illustrate the general principle that ijarah requires a known, deliverable benefit.
5
Derive the mufta bihi
The operative ruling is that hiring a bathhouse is permissible, and specific conditions (like a single entrance) determine validity.
The tarjih authority is the widespread custom and the cited hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وصح أخذ أجرة الحمام) لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم «ما رآه المؤمنون حسناً فهو عند الله حسن» (۱) قال الأكمل: وإنما ذكر هذه في ا الفاسدة أنها جائزة لأن بعض العلماء خالف في ذلك قال الشارح : وبعض العلماء كره الحمام لما روي عنه عليه الصلاة والسلام أنه سماه شر بيت. وقال عثمان : أنه بيت الشيطان. ومن من كرهه للنساء لا للرجال والصحيح أنه لا بأس بالحمامات للرجال والنساء وفي الخلاصة : استأجر حماماً في قرية فوقع الجلاء في القرية ونفر الناس سقطت الأجرة، أو نفر بعض الناس لا تسقط. وفي المحيط : إذا كان حمام للرجال وحمام للنساء فأجرهما جميعاً حماماً جاز استحساناً إذا كان باب الحمامين واحداً، وإن كان لكل واحد وسمي باب على حدة لا يجوز العقد .اهـ. وفي الخلاصة : استأجر حماماً ببدل على أن عليه الأجرة حال جريان الماء وانقطاعه فالإجارة فاسدة. وفي الخانية شيل الرماد والسرقين وتفريغ موضع البالوغة وغيرها على المستأجر فإن شرط على المؤجر فسدت .اهـ. وقال في المحيط : ولو امتلأ مسيل ماء الحمام فعلى المستأجر تفريغه ولو امتلأت البالوعة فعلى الآجر تفريغها، والفرق أن تفريغ مسيل الماء يمكن من غير نقض البناء، وأما البالوعة فلا يمكن تفريغها بنفسه إلا بنقض شيء من البناء ولا يملك المستأجر نقض شيء من البناء وإنما يملكه رب الأرض فجعل تفريغه عليه . وفيه أيضاً : استأجر حمامين سنة فانهدم أحدهما قبل القبض فله ترك الباقي لأن الصفقة تفرقت عليه قبل التمام بخلاف ما لو استأجر حماماً سنة فلم يسلمه إلى المستأجر حتى مضى شهران ولم ينتفع وامتنع المستأجر من القبض فإنه يجبر على القبض ولا يخير لأن الصفقة هنا تفرقت في حق المنافع فلا يوجب ثبوت الخيار وهناك في القبض، وإذا انهدم الحمام قبل القبض فله الخيار ولو انهدم أحد الحمامين بعد القبض فالباقي لازم بحصته لأن الصفقة تفرقت بعد التمام استأجر حماماً وعبداً ليقوم عليه فانهدم الحمام بعد قبضهما فله ترك العبد لأنه عجز عن استعمال العبد فيما استأجره له. وإن هلك العبد فليس له ترك الحمام لأن هلاك العبد لا يوجب خللاً في منفعة الحمام . استأجر الحمام ودخل بنورة أو من رب الحمام يجوز استحساناً . استأجر حماماً بغير قدر واستأجر القدر من آخر فانكسر القدر بعد شهر فأجرة الحمام لازمة دون أجرة القدر لأنه يمكنه أن يستأجر قدراً غيره ويستعمله في الحمام استأجر حماماً شهراً فعمل فيه من الشهر الثاني فلا أجر عليه في الشهر الثاني، وروي عن أصحابنا أن عليه أجرة الشهر الثاني للعرف . قال رحمه الله : ( والحجام) أي جاز أخذ أجرة الحجام لما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام احتجم وأعطى أجرته وبه جرى التعارف بين الناس من لدن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى يومنا هذا فانعقد إجماعاً. وقالت الظاهرية : لا يجوز لما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام نهى عن عسب التيس وكسب الحجام وقفيز الطحان قلنا هذا الحديث منسوخ لما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قال له رجل: إن لي عيالاً وغلاماً حجاماً أفأطعم عيالي من كسبه؟ قال: نعم. وإنما فسرنا الصحة بالجواز لأن العادة جارية هنا وفيما بعده لعدم جريان عقد فيه . قال (لا أجرة عسب التيس) يعني لا يجوز أخذ أجرة عسب التيس لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «إن السحت عسبب التيس مهر البغي» ولأنه عمل لا يقدر عليه وهو الإحبال فلا يجوز أخذ الأجرة عليه ولا أخذ المال بمقابلة الماء وهو نجس لا قيمة له فلا يجوز . والمراد هنا استئجار التيس لينزو على الغنم ويحبلها بأجر، أما لو فعل ذلك من غير أجر لا بأس به لأن به يبقى النسل. وفي المحيط : ومهر البغي في الحديث وهو أن يؤاجر أمته على الزنا وما أخذه من المهر فهو حرام عندهما، وعند الإمام إن أخذه بغير عقد بأن زنى بأمته ثم أعطاها شيئاً فهو حرام لأنه أخذه بغير حق، وإن استأجرها ليزني بها ثم أعطاها مهرها أو ما شرط لها لا بأس بأخذه لأنه في إجارة فاسدة فيطيب له وإن كان السبب حراماً
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And it is valid to take the wage of the bathhouse) due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'What the Muslims see as good is good in the sight of Allah.' Al-Akmal said: He only mentioned this in the chapter of corrupt Ijarah that it is permissible because some scholars differed on that. The commentator said: Some scholars disliked the bathhouse because it is reported that he, peace be upon him, called it the worst house. And Uthman said it is the house of the devil. And some disliked it for women, not men. The correct view is that there is no harm in bathhouses for men and women. In al-Khulasa: If one hires a bathhouse in a village and then a plague occurs and people flee, the wage is dropped; if some flee, not all, the wage is not dropped. In al-Muhit: If there is a bathhouse for men and a bathhouse for women, hiring both as one bathhouse is permissible by istihsan if the door of the two bathhouses is one; if each has a separate door, the contract is not valid. In al-Khulasa: If one hires a bathhouse for a wage on the condition that he pays the wage whether water is flowing or not, the ijarah is fasid. In al-Khaniyya: Removing ashes, dung, and emptying the cesspool are on the lessee; if he stipulates them on the lessor, the ijarah becomes fasid. In al-Muhit: If the water channel of the bathhouse becomes blocked, the lessee must clear it; if the cesspool is full, the lessor must clear it, and the distinction is that clearing the water channel is possible without demolishing the building, while the cesspool requires demolition which the lessee cannot do. And also: If one hires two bathhouses for a year and one collapses before delivery, he may cancel the remaining; but if one hires a bathhouse for a year and the lessor delays delivery for two months and the lessee refuses to take delivery, he is compelled to accept and not given a choice; if the bathhouse collapses before delivery, he has a choice; if one of the two bathhouses collapses after delivery, the remaining is binding for its share. If one hires a bathhouse and a slave to serve in it, and the bathhouse collapses after taking possession of both, he may cancel the slave because he cannot use the slave; if the slave dies, he cannot cancel the bathhouse. If one hires a bathhouse without a boiler and hires a boiler from someone else, and the boiler breaks after a month, the wage for the bathhouse remains due but not for the boiler. If one hires a bathhouse for a month and works for part of the second month, there is no wage for the second month; it is reported from our companions that he owes the wage for the second month according to custom. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And the cupper) meaning it is valid to take the wage of the cupper because it is reported that he, peace be upon him, was cupped and paid his wage, and custom has been ongoing from the time of the Messenger of Allah until today, so consensus has formed. The Zahiris say it is not valid because of the report that he forbade the stud fee of the ram, the earning of the cupper, and the measure of the miller. We say this hadith is abrogated because it is reported that a man said to him: I have dependents and a slave who is a cupper, may I feed my dependents from his earnings? He said: Yes. And we interpret validity as permissibility because custom is current here and in what follows due to the lack of a formal contract. He said: (No wage for the stud fee of the ram) meaning it is not permissible to take a wage for the stud fee of the ram due to his saying: 'Usury is the stud fee of the ram, the dowry of the prostitute,' and because it is an act that cannot be guaranteed, i.e., insemination, so taking a wage for it is not permissible, nor is taking money in exchange for the semen, which is impure and has no value. What is meant here is hiring the ram to mount the sheep and impregnate them for a fee; but if it is done without a fee, there is no harm because the offspring continues. In al-Muhit: The dowry of the prostitute in the hadith is that one hires his slave woman for fornication, and whatever he takes as dowry is forbidden according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad); according to Imam Abu Hanifa, if he takes it without a contract, it is forbidden; but if he hires her for fornication and then gives her dowry or what he stipulated, there is no harm in taking it because it is in a fasid ijarah, so it becomes permissible even if the cause is forbidden.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage covers three interrelated rulings from Kanz al-Daqa'iq: the permissibility of taking wages for hiring a bathhouse (hammam) and cupping (hijamah), and the prohibition of taking wages for stud fees (asbab al-tays). The commentator provides proofs from hadith, custom, and consensus. For the bathhouse, the hadith 'What Muslims see as good is good with Allah' supports the validity, and the commentator notes that some disliked bathhouses but the correct view is permissibility. Numerous subsidiary issues are discussed: if a village is depopulated due to plague, the wage falls; if only some flee, it does not. Hiring separate male and female bathhouses as one is valid by istihsan only if they share a single entrance. Improper conditions (like paying regardless of water flow, or assigning cleaning of certain items to the lessor) render the ijarah fasid. The distinction between clearing water channels (lessee) and cesspools (lessor) is based on the need to demolish the building, which only the owner may do. If a hired bathhouse collapses before delivery, the lessee may cancel the remaining; if after delivery, the remaining is binding. For cupping, the Prophet's practice and continuous custom constitute a consensus that overrides the Zahiri objection based on a hadith that they argue is abrogated. For stud fees, the hadith explicitly calls it usury, and the reasoning is that insemination cannot be guaranteed and the semen is impure. The text also discusses the related issue of the dowry of a prostitute (mahr al-baghi), where Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes between taking money without a contract (haram) and under a fasid ijarah (halal because it falls under a defective contract).

Key Terms
الحمام (al-hammam): Public bathhouse; hiring it is valid per Hanafi school.
الجلاء (al-jala'): A plague or calamity that causes complete evacuation of a locality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What condition must be met for hiring separate men's and women's bathhouses as one unit to be valid?
A) They must have separate boilers.
B) They must share a single entrance.
C) They must be in the same building.
D) The lessee must be a male.

Key Takeaway
Custom and Muslim consensus, as indicated by the hadith, form a valid basis for permissibility in Hanafi fiqh, even when impurities are involved.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
beginner
6 min
Permissibility of Wages for Cupping (Hijamah)
Ruling on cupping wages with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits taking wages for cupping, cite the evidence, and refute the Zahiri objection.

Core Idea
The Prophet paid for cupping and continuous practice forms a consensus that overrides isolated prohibitions.

The second ruling in this passage concerns cupping (hijamah). The Hanafi school holds that it is permissible to take wages for cupping, supported by the Prophet's own practice and the uninterrupted custom of the Muslim community. This lesson examines the proof, the Zahiri objection, and the Hanafi response based on abrogation.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The matn states it is valid to take the wage of the cupper. The commentary explains that validity here means permissibility (jawaz) because custom is the basis.
The ruling is mubah, not wajib or mandub.
2
Identify the Hanafi proof
The author provides two proofs: 1) The Prophet was cupped and paid the cupper. 2) Custom has been continuous from his time to today, forming a consensus (ijma).
The proof combines sunnah fi'liyya (the Prophet's action) and ijma.
3
Understand the Zahiri objection
The Zahiris cite a hadith that the Prophet forbade the earnings of the cupper (among other things). They argue it is haram.
The same hadith also prohibits the stud fee of the ram.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school argues that the prohibition hadith is abrogated (mansukh) by a later hadith where the Prophet allowed feeding one's family from the cupper's earnings.
The principle is that a later, specific permission overrides an earlier general prohibition.
5
Conclude with mufta bihi
The Hanafi view is the operative position (mufta bihi) due to the strength of the proof and the absence of a reliable counterproof.
This is a clear example of inter-madhhab ikhtilaf resolved by abrogation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وصح أخذ أجرة الحمام) لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم «ما رآه المؤمنون حسناً فهو عند الله حسن» (۱) قال الأكمل: وإنما ذكر هذه في ا الفاسدة أنها جائزة لأن بعض العلماء خالف في ذلك قال الشارح : وبعض العلماء كره الحمام لما روي عنه عليه الصلاة والسلام أنه سماه شر بيت. وقال عثمان : أنه بيت الشيطان. ومن من كرهه للنساء لا للرجال والصحيح أنه لا بأس بالحمامات للرجال والنساء وفي الخلاصة : استأجر حماماً في قرية فوقع الجلاء في القرية ونفر الناس سقطت الأجرة، أو نفر بعض الناس لا تسقط. وفي المحيط : إذا كان حمام للرجال وحمام للنساء فأجرهما جميعاً حماماً جاز استحساناً إذا كان باب الحمامين واحداً، وإن كان لكل واحد وسمي باب على حدة لا يجوز العقد .اهـ. وفي الخلاصة : استأجر حماماً ببدل على أن عليه الأجرة حال جريان الماء وانقطاعه فالإجارة فاسدة. وفي الخانية شيل الرماد والسرقين وتفريغ موضع البالوغة وغيرها على المستأجر فإن شرط على المؤجر فسدت .اهـ. وقال في المحيط : ولو امتلأ مسيل ماء الحمام فعلى المستأجر تفريغه ولو امتلأت البالوعة فعلى الآجر تفريغها، والفرق أن تفريغ مسيل الماء يمكن من غير نقض البناء، وأما البالوعة فلا يمكن تفريغها بنفسه إلا بنقض شيء من البناء ولا يملك المستأجر نقض شيء من البناء وإنما يملكه رب الأرض فجعل تفريغه عليه . وفيه أيضاً : استأجر حمامين سنة فانهدم أحدهما قبل القبض فله ترك الباقي لأن الصفقة تفرقت عليه قبل التمام بخلاف ما لو استأجر حماماً سنة فلم يسلمه إلى المستأجر حتى مضى شهران ولم ينتفع وامتنع المستأجر من القبض فإنه يجبر على القبض ولا يخير لأن الصفقة هنا تفرقت في حق المنافع فلا يوجب ثبوت الخيار وهناك في القبض، وإذا انهدم الحمام قبل القبض فله الخيار ولو انهدم أحد الحمامين بعد القبض فالباقي لازم بحصته لأن الصفقة تفرقت بعد التمام استأجر حماماً وعبداً ليقوم عليه فانهدم الحمام بعد قبضهما فله ترك العبد لأنه عجز عن استعمال العبد فيما استأجره له. وإن هلك العبد فليس له ترك الحمام لأن هلاك العبد لا يوجب خللاً في منفعة الحمام . استأجر الحمام ودخل بنورة أو من رب فيه من الشهر الثاني فلا أجر عليه في الشهر الثاني، وروي عن أصحابنا أن عليه أجرة الشهر الثاني للعرف . قال رحمه الله : ( والحجام) أي جاز أخذ أجرة الحجام لما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام احتجم وأعطى أجرته وبه جرى التعارف بين الناس من لدن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى يومنا هذا فانعقد إجماعاً. وقالت الظاهرية : لا يجوز لما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام نهى عن عسب التيس وكسب الحجام وقفيز الطحان قلنا هذا الحديث منسوخ لما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قال له رجل: إن لي عيالاً وغلاماً حجاماً أفأطعم عيالي من كسبه؟ قال: نعم. وإنما فسرنا الصحة بالجواز لأن العادة جارية هنا وفيما بعده لعدم جريان عقد فيه . قال (لا أجرة عسب التيس) يعني لا يجوز أخذ أجرة عسب التيس لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «إن السحت عسبب التيس مهر البغي» ولأنه عمل لا يقدر عليه وهو الإحبال فلا يجوز أخذ الأجرة عليه ولا أخذ المال بمقابلة الماء وهو نجس لا قيمة له فلا يجوز . والمراد هنا استئجار التيس لينزو على الغنم ويحبلها بأجر، أما لو فعل ذلك من غير أجر لا بأس به لأن به يبقى النسل. وفي المحيط : ومهر البغي في الحديث وهو أن يؤاجر أمته على الزنا وما أخذه من المهر فهو حرام عندهما، وعند الإمام إن أخذه بغير عقد بأن زنى بأمته ثم أعطاها شيئاً فهو حرام لأنه أخذه بغير حق، وإن استأجرها ليزني بها ثم أعطاها مهرها أو ما شرط لها لا بأس بأخذه لأنه في إجارة فاسدة فيطيب له وإن كان السبب حراماً
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And it is valid to take the wage of the bathhouse) due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'What the Muslims see as good is good in the sight of Allah.' Al-Akmal said: He only mentioned this in the chapter of corrupt Ijarah that it is permissible because some scholars differed on that. The commentator said: Some scholars disliked the bathhouse because it is reported that he, peace be upon him, called it the worst house. And Uthman said it is the house of the devil. If one hires a bathhouse for a month and works for part of the second month, there is no wage for the second month; it is reported from our companions that he owes the wage for the second month according to custom. Commentary
This passage covers three interrelated rulings from Kanz al-Daqa'iq: the permissibility of taking wages for hiring a bathhouse (hammam) and cupping (hijamah), and the prohibition of taking wages for stud fees (asbab al-tays). The commentator provides proofs from hadith, custom, and consensus. For the bathhouse, the hadith 'What Muslims see as good is good with Allah' supports the validity, and the commentator notes that some disliked bathhouses but the correct view is permissibility. Numerous subsidiary issues are discussed: if a village is depopulated due to plague, the wage falls; if only some flee, it does not. Hiring separate male and female bathhouses as one is valid by istihsan only if they share a single entrance. Improper conditions (like paying regardless of water flow, or assigning cleaning of certain items to the lessor) render the ijarah fasid. The distinction between clearing water channels (lessee) and cesspools (lessor) is based on the need to demolish the building, which only the owner may do. If a hired bathhouse collapses before delivery, the lessee may cancel the remaining; if after delivery, the remaining is binding. For cupping, the Prophet's practice and continuous custom constitute a consensus that overrides the Zahiri objection based on a hadith that they argue is abrogated. For stud fees, the hadith explicitly calls it usury, and the reasoning is that insemination cannot be guaranteed and the semen is impure. The text also discusses the related issue of the dowry of a prostitute (mahr al-baghi), where Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes between taking money without a contract (haram) and under a fasid ijarah (halal because it falls under a defective contract).

Key Terms
الحجام (al-hajjam): A cupper; a profession whose wages are permissible.
منسوخ (mansukh): Abrogated – a ruling that has been superseded by a later revelation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi basis for abrogating the hadith forbidding the cupper's earnings?
A) A stronger Quranic verse.
B) A later hadith where the Prophet allowed feeding family from cupper earnings.
C) Consensus of the Companions.
D) The fact that cupping is a medical necessity.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's practice and continuous consensus overrides an isolated prohibition, especially when an explicit later permission exists.
